### Post by arniev on 2005-10-11
Ewan ko because I'm still new with linux and ubuntu pero naconfig nya internet connection ko using a linksys router. Dapat siguro config mo muna pppoe mo.

the command is:

sudo pppoeconf

tapos punta ka sa networking at i-activate mo ung ethernet card mo.

Install ko kasi ubuntu minus the network installation dahil di ko pa configure router ko. pero nung na configure sya sa windows I was amazed na na configure din sya sa ubuntu.

btw, pati wireless connection sa laptop configure din nya. Galing talaga ng ubuntu.

Well I hope this help. But if it does not, what do I know? I'm just a newbie here.

### Post by Kapre on 2005-10-14
[QUOTE=redenjaja]guys may command ba para mag automount yung hdd na naka ntfs format? para pag boot ko sa ubuntu eh mounted na kagad sya?[/QUOTE]

reden - walang command na kailangan. Pero siguraduhin mo lang na naka declare sya sa fstab mo para pag-reboot/login mo ay automagic na syang mounted. Click mo itong use ME sa sig ko then look for the mount ntfs.

Try mo rin itong "sudo mount -a"

### Post by jeffreyvergara.NET on 2005-10-18
hehehe... almost same tau PC akin p4 2.o lng, ska fx5200 rin, pero 786 lng mem ko...

@MakubeX, fan k nang get backers no? wahehehe
Ph din gamit ko repo pero ok din naman, try mo replace http:// with ftp:// ganan ginawa ko sken dati, pero ok naman speed ng PH repo ko kahit http:// ngaun..

> #deb cdrom:[Ubuntu 5.10 _Breezy Badger_ - Release i386 (20051012)]/ breezy main restricted


## Uncomment the following two lines to fetch updated software from the network
deb [http://ph.archive.ubuntu.com/ubuntu](http://ph.archive.ubuntu.com/ubuntu) breezy main restricted
deb-src [http://ph.archive.ubuntu.com/ubuntu](http://ph.archive.ubuntu.com/ubuntu) breezy main restricted

## Uncomment the following two lines to fetch major bug fix updates produced
## after the final release of the distribution.
deb [http://ph.archive.ubuntu.com/ubuntu](http://ph.archive.ubuntu.com/ubuntu) breezy-updates main restricted
deb-src [http://ph.archive.ubuntu.com/ubuntu](http://ph.archive.ubuntu.com/ubuntu) breezy-updates main restricted

## Uncomment the following two lines to add software from the 'universe'
## repository.
## N.B. software from this repository is ENTIRELY UNSUPPORTED by the Ubuntu
## team, and may not be under a free licence. Please satisfy yourself as to
## your rights to use the software. Also, please note that software in
## universe WILL NOT receive any review or updates from the Ubuntu security
## team.
deb [http://ph.archive.ubuntu.com/ubuntu](http://ph.archive.ubuntu.com/ubuntu) breezy universe
deb-src [http://ph.archive.ubuntu.com/ubuntu](http://ph.archive.ubuntu.com/ubuntu) breezy universe

## Uncomment the following two lines to add software from the 'backports'
## repository.
## N.B. software from this repository may not have been tested as
## extensively as that contained in the main release, although it includes
## newer versions of some applications which may provide useful features.
## Also, please note that software in backports WILL NOT receive any review
## or updates from the Ubuntu security team.
#deb [http://ph.archive.ubuntu.com/ubuntu](http://ph.archive.ubuntu.com/ubuntu) breezy-backports main restricted universe multiverse
#deb-src [http://ph.archive.ubuntu.com/ubuntu](http://ph.archive.ubuntu.com/ubuntu) breezy-backports main restricted universe multiverse

deb [http://ph.archive.ubuntu.com/ubuntu](http://ph.archive.ubuntu.com/ubuntu) breezy universe
deb-src [http://ph.archive.ubuntu.com/ubuntu](http://ph.archive.ubuntu.com/ubuntu) breezy universe

deb [http://security.ubuntu.com/ubuntu](http://security.ubuntu.com/ubuntu) breezy-security main restricted
deb-src [http://security.ubuntu.com/ubuntu](http://security.ubuntu.com/ubuntu) breezy-security main restricted

deb [http://security.ubuntu.com/ubuntu](http://security.ubuntu.com/ubuntu) breezy-security universe
deb-src [http://security.ubuntu.com/ubuntu](http://security.ubuntu.com/ubuntu) breezy-security universe


deb [http://archive.ubuntu.com/ubuntu](http://archive.ubuntu.com/ubuntu) breezy multiverse
deb-src [http://archive.ubuntu.com/ubuntu](http://archive.ubuntu.com/ubuntu) breezy multiverse

### Post by jeffreyvergara.NET on 2005-10-20
wahehe meron na pala fix dun sa bug ng translation

> > Meron sa tanong kapag nag install ka gamit ang terminal kung "Oo / Hindi"
> [O/h] pero mali pag ang ginamit mo eh O or H, dapat y or n

Eric Pareja wrote: 
Ito ay kilalang bug sa paketeng locales at naiulat na sa upstream
bilang Debian Bug #295810. Naka-binbin na lamang ito sa mismong
pinagmulan ng locales (glibc source) na upstream pa, na medyo
konserbatibo ang pag-angkat ng pagbabago sa talaksang pang-datos.

Inayos namin ito sa Debian sa pamamagitan ng belocs-locales-bin
package na maaari ninyong iluklok.

# apt-get install belocs-locales-bin

### Post by bonjun on 2005-10-22
guys, anong na-encounter na mga bug/errors sa Breezy at anong fix ang ginawa o nakita nyo dito sa forum 


sa akin floppy lang, 
> Error: given UDI is not a mountable volume.

at ito yong fix na nasearch ko sa forum

Code:
> ln -sf /usr/bin/pmount /usr/bin/pmount-hal

from this [thread]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=70196&")


post nyo din yong mga errors/bugs and fix/es na na-encounter nyo para madali ng maghanap ang mga kapwa natin pinoy

### Post by jsgotangco on 2005-10-23
Try it out yourself :) It supports a good number of markup languages.

My issue with Nvu is that its basically Mozilla composer with a few tweaks. It's also one reason why its not promoted to main, is because the distro will have two instances of Mozilla installed..with different versions I believe...so in a support mindset, Ubuntu will be supporting two versions of Mozilla...which isn't a good idea...

In my opinion, Quanta Plus is much better than Nvu though :)

anyways... I just want to share na meron pala fix sa eject button ng CD/DVD Drives.. para hindi na rightclick sa Drive para mag eject..

sudo sh -c 'echo "dev.cdrom.lock=0" >> /etc/sysctl.conf'

### Post by jsgotangco on 2005-10-28
install ubuntu as server (or base install)

edit your sources.list (/etc/apt/sources.list) and enable universe

then on console do:

```
sudo apt-get update
sudo apt-getinstall xubuntu-desktop
```

batangas@ubuntu:~$ tar xzf automatix-breezy.tar.gz
tar: automatix-breezy.tar.gz: Cannot open: No such file or directory

### Post by jeffreyvergara.NET on 2005-10-30
kung saan folder mo sinave ung automatix
e.g. /home/username/

tar xzf automatix-breezy-versionnumberhere.tar.gz

pag nasa home directory mo ung autmatix.tar.gz type mo lang "tar zxf autamatixversion.tar.gz

tapos cd /home/username/autamatix

then ./install

BTW, ito ang gamit namin kung xDSL at ethernet ang connection, pero kung USB ay hindi ko na masasagot (most of the post - although Speedtouch USB - ay nahihirapan sila mag-connect).

### Post by jsgotangco on 2005-10-30
[QUOTE=jeffreyvergara.NET]just like symantic does.. ^_^ - backports i think.
[/QUOTE]

You don't need it then. Your sources.list in Ubuntu 5.10 (Breezy) already has ubuntu backports listed only needs to be uncommented (along with universe and multiverse).

```
sudo gedit /etc/apt/sources.list
```

### Post by jsgotangco on 2005-10-31
[QUOTE=Big Venus]At my school, we use Windows practically every where except the Linux class, which uses Fedora Core 4. I personally at home still use Windows on all of my systems. The only time I use Linux is when I want to have fun learning something new or just want to feel alittle geekie... So to speak.[/QUOTE]

Well i know a lot of people who use Linux everyday - and they're no geeks at all. Some of them are accountants, lawyers, even some government people. Desktop usage is increasing because the applications are more mature now. 8 years ago, you have to manually configure XFree86 to have a working desktop. Installing Linux now is sometimes much easier than installing Windows. The simplicity of the GNOME desktop makes it appealing to newcomers. Some also like the cheerful, bubbly appearance of KDE. With the upcoming desktop initiatives expect major improvements to your desktop experience.

### Post by pinoyskull on 2005-11-01
[QUOTE=jsgotangco]What does Automatix do specifically?[/QUOTE]
it just automates your installation of applications

here's a snippet of the automatix code
```

function multimedia {
        # Install multimedia packages
        apt-get --assume-yes --force-yes install totem-xine gstreamer0.8-plugins gstreamer0.8-lame gstreamer0.8-ffmpeg gstreamer0.8-faac gstreamer0.8-faad libxvidcore4 lame sox ffmpeg mjpegtools vorbis-tools mpg321 | zenity --progress --pulsate --auto-close --title "Automatix" --text $"Installing multimedia packages"
        gst-register-0.8 | zenity --progress --pulsate --auto-close --title "Automatix" --text $"Registering new codecs"

}

function soundconf {
        # Change esd and asd conf files
        if zenity --warning --title "Automatix" --text $" First go to System->Preferences->Sound and disable 'Enable Sound Server Startup' and then hit OK"
        then
                apt-get --assume-yes --force-yes install libesd-alsa0
                mv -f /etc/esound/esd.conf /etc/esound/esd.conf_backup
                mv -f /etc/asound.conf /etc/asound.conf_backup
                cp /usr/local/automatix/conf/esd.conf /etc/esound/esd.conf
                cp /usr/local/automatix/conf/asound.conf /etc/asound.conf
                cp /usr/local/automatix/conf/libao.conf /etc/libao.conf
        fi

}

```

---

### Post by MakubeX on 2005-11-04
[QUOTE=pinoyskull]chix rox! i just installed it and tried it, it worked, although a couple of times my GAIM crashed, but still its a good program[/QUOTE]

Here's the tip.. from my experience, Gaim (with Chix) will only crash if you send a message to a number/contact that is not yet on the list. The workaround that I do is to register the number via Javalite (exiting Chix), add the contact there, and relogin in the Chix. Try it. It never crashed/exited again after learning/discovering that bug.

Well, chikka-gaim doesn't have PC-PC interaction yet.

### Post by pinoyskull on 2005-11-09
[QUOTE=squibbon]di ko mapagana Chix sa gaim. nainstall ko na siya pero di ako makalogin...
ginamit ko account ko sa chikka, try ko na rin email add ko pero wala talaga. tulong naman o.
[/QUOTE]
paano mo ba ininstall ang chix, 2 packages kailangan mo kasi, yung **libchix_1.0.0-1_i386.deb** tsaka **libchixgaim_1.0.0-1_i386.deb**, after mo ma install start/restart gaim, open mo gaim>tools>accounts, tapos add ka account, dapat sa protocol list meron ka makikita na chix, kung wala may problema installatin mo, try mo ulitin, sa screen name dapat **63<cellnumber>** without the leading 0, tapos password, you're done!

---

### Post by jsgotangco on 2005-11-13

As for mounting your partitions to Ubuntu, refer to the Ubuntu 5.10 Starter Guide, by clicking System -> Help.

### Post by MakubeX on 2005-11-13
Re: Chix

Adjust the port number.. you'll only know that chix installed successfully as a protocol of Gaim if you see it in the list of protocols (obviously). Next problem is the port number.. some networks have blocked some ports or have some alternative port numbers for such protocols. In the case of Javalite - AFAIK, you can't adjust its port number. From observation, I assume that Javalite uses port 6301 by default.

### Post by jsgotangco on 2005-11-14

---

### Post by jsgotangco on 2005-11-14
[QUOTE=squibbon]anong mas ok sa tingin nyo Ubuntu o Kubuntu? tanong ko lang kz gusto ko rin KDE kz meron clang kdevelop at QT3. meron po akong cedega at point2play pero di ko pa nasubukan. meron bang may ganon dito?

Dapper Drake di ba meron ng GNOME at KDE? correct me if i'm wrong. i can't wait to get my hands on it.[/QUOTE]


Ubuntu and Kubuntu share both the same base, except that both of them have different default installs. If you're using for an equivalent to kdevelop in GNOME, there's Anjuta and Monodevelop for starters. QT3 is no different from GTK, both are toolkits for a specific purpose.

As for Dapper Drake, this is the development branch and yes, both still have GNOME and KDE on Main and it'll be out on April 2006.

---

### Post by bonjun on 2005-11-18
[QUOTE=sherwindennis]fellow filipino ubuntu user....patulong naman po...

I already installed jre1.5.0_05 but still I cannot use chikka javalite. 
I have this output when running 'java -version'
______________

java version "1.5.0_05"
Java(TM) 2 Runtime Environment, Standard Edition (build 1.5.0_05-b05)
Java HotSpot(TM) Client VM (build 1.5.0_05-b05, mixed mode, sharing)
______________

Please help me....Thanks in advance![/QUOTE]


Link your plugins to firefox :

> sudo ln -s /usr/local/java/jre1.5.0_05/plugin/i386/ns7/libjavaplugin_oji.so /usr/lib/mozilla-firefox/plugins

to verify: 
Run Firefox and type: 
> about:plugins

### Post by MakubeX on 2005-11-30
[QUOTE=bonjun]done that..

btw, here is the error in mounting[/QUOTE]

Maybe the device doesn't really exist. There was a time when I troubleshooted in our rental PCs, i tried mounting the floppy, but it says that the device doesn't exist. Later, I found out that the floppy disk was not really inserted/plugged to the hardware, sheesh.

Or maybe (in your case) the floppy drive is not connected? (loose?)

### Post by bonjun on 2005-12-03
[QUOTE=bionnaki]I'm sure this has been asked in this here mammoth 89 page thread, but...what the heck is pinoy?[/QUOTE]

here is your answer sir:
> 
Pinoy
From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia.

Pinoy is a term used by Filipinos for their compatriots in the Philippines and around the world. Filipinos usually refer to themselves informally as Pinoy (feminine: Pinay), which is formed by taking the four letters in the middle of Pilipino and adding the diminutive suffix -y. The word was coined by expatriate Filipino Americans during the 1920s and was later adopted by Filipinos in the Philippines.

Pinoy is a term of endearment and is rarely used in formal settings. The term is akin to that of a nickname which is used by close family members and friends so that one who uses it somehow already developed some close ties with Filipinos.

The term especially gained popular currency in the late 1970s in the Philippines when a surge in patriotism made a hit song of Filipino folksinger Heber Bartolome's "Tayo'y mga Pinoy" (We are Filipinos).

However, in the United States, some Americans of Filipino descent dislike the term. Many of them prefer rather to use the more formal "Filipino".

from [http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pinoy]("http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pinoy")


this one explains better, than what i have in mind,  peace bro...Mabuhay!!!

### Post by jeffreyvergara.NET on 2005-12-11
@hack_jammer1998 cge bro txt nlng kita kapag nkuha ko na ung package ko, medyo madami ata un ngaun. kung alam mo ang Enzo Electromart mas ok.. hehehe

@jdash - ilagay mo sa /home folder mo ung installer para ma execute mo sa terminal ung command para ma install ang modem
> e.g. username@networkname:-$
or pwede mo rin execute :
> username@networkname:-$ cd Desktop/
kung ayaw mo sa home.. heheh..

meron na mura aDSL diba, 1k/month - unlimited, recommended kung heavy Internet user ka, pero kung casual lng, ok na dial-up. meron pala ako nabasa na mas madali i-setup ang External modem sa Linux kaysa sa Internal modems, parang plug & play lang daw. saka ung conexant na modem, kung sa Linuxant mo nakuha ung installer, mababa lng daw speed ang available, kelangan pa ata magbayad para ma access mo ang 56kbps na speed. pero kung kaya mo aDSL mas maganda para mas magamit mo ng maayos ubuntu, madami kasi packages na kelangan talaga Internet.

### Post by bonjun on 2005-12-14
pipol i nid ur help,,, may isa akong pc, pag-reboot/shutdown/restart (whatever), laging nawawala ang setting ng network niya, kaya lagi akong add ng setting ng network thru **/sbin/ifconfig** & **/sbin/route**, breezy ang OS with xubuntu ang desktop,,, san ba ang setting para permanente na ang network,, tenks in adbans...

---

### Post by pinoyskull on 2005-12-14
@bonjun

for permanent settings, put it in **/etc/network/interfaces**

---

### Post by bonjun on 2005-12-14
[QUOTE=pinoyskull]@bonjun

for permanent settings, put it in **/etc/network/interfaces**[/QUOTE]
it has the setting of my network:
> user@pc:~$ cat /etc/network/interfaces
# This file describes the network interfaces available on your system
# and how to activate them. For more information, see interfaces(5).

# The loopback network interface
auto lo
iface lo inet loopback

# This is a list of hotpluggable network interfaces.
# They will be activated automatically by the hotplug subsystem.
mapping hotplug
        script grep
        map eth0

# The primary network interface
iface eth0 inet static
        address 192.168.0.6
        netmask 255.255.255.0
        network 192.168.x.x
        broadcast 192.168.x.x
        gateway 192.168.x.x
        # dns-* options are implemented by the resolvconf package, if installed
        dns-nameservers 202.x.x.x 202.x.x.x
(note:edited)
even before i add my setting at /sbin/ifconfig & /sbin/route

### Post by geonetrinity on 2005-12-23
Mabuhay!!!

ORIGINAL PINOY CONCEPT!!! ORIGINAL PINOY CONCEPT!!! ORIGINAL PINOY CONCEPT!!!

Kung narinig nyo na yung AUTOMATIX, kaya nito mag-install ng mga importanteng files ng hindi ka na nagkoconfigure sa terminal GUI fronted click and wait ka lang automated lahat, pero kailangan ng internet, pag walang internet di ito gagana.

Counterpart nito...

Natapos ko na yung terminal base script, na may kakayahang mag-install ng hindi na kailangan ng internet. BURNED-ON-CD na, hindi nga ito GUI front pero simple lang ang gagawin mo, kokopyahin mo lang script installer sa home/user folder mo at irun mo sa terminal (./geone.sh) wait ka lang hanggang matoposka. Kool, eto YUNG MGA GAGAWIN NYA:

	Package update for ubuntu breezy badger, multimedia codecs para maplay mo yung mp3, wav, movies at etc, binura ko yung totem gstreamer, at pinalitan ko ng totem xine para magamit mo si totem sa movies and sound (take note TOTEM), Kde basepackage for crossplatform, abiword 2.4.1., gnumeric 1.5.9., msfonts compatibility, AMAROK working gnome, at eto pa JAVA AND FLASH. Camorama, digikam, f-spot, inkscape, winrar, azureus, adobe acrobat, d4x, gnomeppp/kppp, LIMEWIRE & SKYPE (VoIP), gnomebaker, easytag, audiotag, soundconverter, kate, gftp. Amule, Xmms, Mplayer, alien, gparted, Opera browser at audacity.

	Kinostomize ko rin yung mga splash screen, Gnome Splash, Gimp Splash at OpenOffice splash, binago ko lahat throung script.

	mga di ko nailagay: fstab windows compatibility script at floppy mounter, programming files, siguro future plans na lang... sobrang dami na nyan. Insallation will take 10-15mins on my unit.  Ang laki ng nasave mong time sa ibat-ibang terminal configuration. (almost 1-2hrs kang nagkoconfigure!!!!)

Kool diba, Okey till next time mga tol.


geonetrinity...
"let's make a beginnings with LINUX"

MGA TOL PATI KERNEL NA-UPDATE KO (maging yung mga latest package sa distrowatch yung release na naupdate ko, packages po!!! hindi OS), automatix naka focus lang sa application and others, manual ang update kailangan pati ng internet.

Balak ko rin magbuo ng another team para gumawa ng mga package cd installers para ibat ibang linux, tulad ng Ubuntu (kde and gnome), fedora redhat 4, yung kool na kool arklinux.  Para may notable contribution tayong mga pinoy sa LINUX. Syempre, malaking hindrance dito #1 (pera) #2 (time).

Di ba limang taon ang support ubuntu, para sa mga updates ang packages, paano kung after nun gusto mo lang ipresent yung old version ng ubuntu kailangan mo ng internet para sa mga packages, yun ang malaking tanong.

parang WINDOW98SE wala ng support para dito terminated na, di ba vulnerable ito sa ibat ibang virus, usual lobby nga ito ng trojans di ba, kung alam nyo lang hehehehe, way back 2001 same thing ang ginagawa ko SA WIN98SE may compilation ako ng LAHAT NG UPDATES ANG PATCHES, pati installer INTERNET EXPLOREr 6 pati updrage packagesng IE6(hindi tracker base installer talaga), compiled ko sa CD, di lang natapos yan sa win98, winME,win2000, win2000sever, even winXP meron ako. I'LL call you jeff pag ready na sa net, yung gaim 2.0 mo CVS lang yun... wait ka ng lang ipapackage ko na rin dun... 
____________________________________________
kailangan mo rin to para gumana Webcam mo:
mag-root ka muna TERMINAL  "SU"

sudo apt-get install linux-headers-`uname -r` linux-restricted-modules-`uname -r` build-essential gcc-3.4

(YUNG "uname -r" kunin mo sa terminal, at yun ang ilagay mo example : 10.12.42.34 sample lang yan ha)

Now do the following one by one:

su
CC=gcc-3.4
export CC
exit
CC=gcc-3.4
export CC
wget [http://mxhaard.free.fr/spca50x/Download/spca5xx-20050906.tar.gz](http://mxhaard.free.fr/spca50x/Download/spca5xx-20050906.tar.gz)
tar xvfz spca5xx-20050906.tar.gz
cd spca5xx-20050906
make
sudo modprobe -r spca5xx
sudo rm -rf /lib/modules/`uname -r`/kernel/drivers/usb/media/spca5xx*
sudo make install
sudo modprobe spca5xx


(kailangan mo rin ito para sa camorama)

Oo nga pala, may isang dean akong nakausap dyan, plano nyang kausapin mga school for serminar drive, taga-batangas wala pa syang reply di ko pa alam kung matutuloy.

### Post by geonetrinity on 2005-12-29
Image Editor 
(close feature ng photoshop)
may bayad nga lang...

[http://www.kanzelsberger.com/pixel/?page_id=12]("http://www.kanzelsberger.com/pixel/?page_id=12")

Pixel is a RGB, CMYK and HDR image editing, photo retouching and manipulating program available for many operating systems formerly known as Pixel32. It is available for Windows, Linux, Linspire, MacOSX, BeOS, Zeta, QNX, MorphOS, FreeBSD, eComStation, OS/2, SkyOS and even old plain DOS, for both x86 and PowerPC architectures.
	
Pixel is not free software, if you like it and want to support its development, you may consider Purchasing a copy. Licensing and prices are very fair, and include unlimited support.
_______________________________________

Features

Pixel has a multiplatform design and looks the same on every supported platform. Also, every file produced with Pixel is cross-platform and can be copied files from one platform to another. This is a feature list for v1.0 final available in September 2005 by latest.

Platforms

    * Pixel is running following platforms now: Windows, Linux/x86, Linux/PPC, Linspire, Zeta/BeOS/x86, QNX/x86, FreeBSD/x86, MacOSX/PPC, MorphOS/PPC, eComStation, OS/2, SkyOS and DOS
    * In future following ports are possible: Linux/x86_64, Linux/ARM, MacOSX/x86

Core

    * Pixel is an extremely small and fast application
    * it is easy to translate to any language as it supports full Unicode, all available translations are available at once (English, German, French, Spanish, Dutch, Slovak, Finnish, Korean, Hungarian and Brazilian Portuguese)
    * IME and XIM support for Asian languages
    * supports TWAIN compatible scanners, digital cameras
    * supports SANE compatible scanners, digital cameras and others (Linux, BeOS, eComStation)
    * pressure sensitive tablets support
    * printing support
    * multiple color managed clipboards
    * various image formats handling (GIF, PNG, JPG, TIFF, BMP, PSD&#8230;)
    * support for JPEG-2000 format

Image editing

    * support for layers, channels, masks and selections
    * Color Management support for RGB, CMYK, Grayscale and CIE Lab modes (8-bit and 16-bit)
    * support for HDR (High Dynamic Range) images with 32-bit/channel precision, HDR images in Pixel are editable in full HDR quality, not in 8-bit RGB as in competiting programs
    * realtime live effects for layers (adjustments, effects), sets of live effects can be saved as layer Styles
    * image browsing and searching

Retouching

    * includes variety of brushes, including full-color brushes and animated brushes
    * brush retouching tools including special effects
    * retouching set of filter plug-ins

Web features

    * complex support for image slicing and image optimizations (GIF, PNG, JPEG, WBMP)
    * direct editing of generated HTML code without destroying user&#8217;s additions
    * support for clickable maps
    * support for small animations for your web pages (animated GIFs)

---

### Post by geonetrinity on 2005-12-29
Krita
Krita Version 1.4.2
© 2000-2005 the Krita Team

To install :
sudo apt-get install krita
____________________________________________

Krita is a painting and image editing application for KOffice. Krita is part of KOffice since 1.4. Krita contains both ease-of-use and fun features like guided painting (never before has it been so easy to airbrush a straight line!) and high-end features like support for 16 bit images, CMYK and even OpenEXR HDR images.

Features

Development on Krita was started in 1999. However, due to frequent changes of maintainer and long pauses between bursts of development wasn't ready for use until 2005. Now Krita is a capable image editor and a great platform for future development. The first public release of Krita (version 1.4.1) has the following features:

    * Painting with brushes and colors
    * Creating brushes from circles and squares
    * Filling with colour, patterns and gradients
    * Erasing
    * Airbrush
    * Simple geometric forms, optionally filled with colours, patterns or gradient.
    * Many filters
    * undo and redo
    * Loading and saving of images in its native file format.
    * Importing and exporting of images in all file formats supported by your installation of ImageMagick.
    * Adding, removing, reordering and merging of layers.
    * Layer transparency.
    * Loading Gimp brushes, pipe brushes, gradients and patterns.
    * Zoom.
    * Color selection.
    * Gray(A), RGB(A) color models.
    * Support for Wacom tablets.
    * High-quality scaling, rotating and shearing.
    * Selections, with a full set of selection tools.
    * A complete color management system based on lcms
    * A cimg-based image restoration tool
    * Histograms
    * And much more...

---

### Post by geonetrinity on 2005-12-29
GTK based 2D Animation software released under GPL
panoorin mo to:
[http://www.bridgetone.com/voria/movies/prologue.mov]("http://www.bridgetone.com/voria/movies/prologue.mov")
A new professional and very powerful 2D animation product has been open sourced after the company behind it failed to find enough customers. Synfig, which uses gtkmm (screenshot), has now been released completely under the GPL and it's still very actively maintained by its original author, Robert Quattlebaum.
_________________________
Download and compile nga lang:
(pero the best talaga)

### Post by lutosdemayo on 2005-12-30
[QUOTE=jeffreyvergara.NET]hindi ko parin maayos network ng Vmware at samba.. Y_Y, ok na sana vmware kaso hindi pwede mag run ng 3d games. Y_Y[/QUOTE]

Ginawa ko pre nag lagay ako ng shared sa /home/username1/SharedFolder at nag create ako ng bagong user say username2 at binigyan ko ng full write permission at i mapped out my /var/www to /home/username1/SharedFolder
para ma access sa windows. Install ka ng webmin para mas madali. I mapped it as network drive sa windows ung /home/username1/SharedFolder at gamitin mo ung 2nd user mo pag logon.

Next tym try ko gumawa ng active directory at mag lagay ako ng maraming windows para masubukan.

### Post by lutosdemayo on 2006-01-04
[QUOTE=jeffreyvergara.NET]tol hindi ko mapagana Dreamweaver 8 using WINE 0.9.3, laging interrupted daw installation[/QUOTE]

Sori pre di ko na ellaborate kung pano gamitin ung dreamweaver 8. instal mo muna sa windows partion ung trial hanapin mo ung crack na may fff sa pangalan at i patch mo. Yung activation kasi ang nag papa crash sa installation. Lipat mo ung dreamweaver 8 na folder sa wine directory mo and run it from the terminal. Ininstal ko sa vmware din pero ung sa wine ang ginagamit ko ngayon parang native speed na kasi lalo na na nag 0.9.4 na ung wine it just get better.

---

### Post by lutosdemayo on 2006-01-04
[QUOTE=jeffreyvergara.NET]pare lutosdemayo pa tutor naman sa networking ubuntu to Window$ via VMWARE player, nag install na ako Samba and configured ko na workgroup = WORKGROUP, para parehas sila ng workgroup ng Window$, pero hindi ma detect ng Window$.

meron na rin ako webmin, pero hindi ko alam gagawin.. Y_Y[/QUOTE]

Pre pasencya na di ako expert gusto ko lang matuto ng linux lahat ng ginagawa ko puro trial and error din pero try mo lang:

1. Mag install ka ng module for samba sa webmin  sudo apt-get install webmin-samba ka sa terminal or sa synaptic mo para mas madali
2. Logon ka sa webmin mo. punta ka sa Servers>Samba Windows File Sharing 
3. Merong mga options dun sa samba users gumawa ka ng isang account say user1. Sychronize mo ung unix at samba users mo.
4. Click mo ung Create a New File Share mag create ka ng shared folder sa loob mismo ng home directory like /home/lutosdemayo/SharedFolder. Binigyan ko ng 777 permission full read and write. 
4. Set mo ung ip-address sa windows like setting a home network. Remember pre na ung windows mo sa vmware as a separate and independent computer. 
5. Now got to the network neighborhood sa windows at browse mo yung share na workgroup click mo yung linuxbox mo at i enter mo ung user1 that you have created and save the password. Para walang hastle mount your shared folder as a network drive para everytime na gamitin mo ung windows nandun na. Transfer ur www-http directory there para either ways linux or windows may read-write permission. 

Yung PC may 1.5G na ram kaya d ko napapansin ung performance drop ng windows pero pag pinatakbo ko ung freebsd and windows server 2003 medyo mabagal na.

Sana pre maka tulong to. Happy Ubuntuing!!! Mabuhay tayong lahat!!!!:razz: :razz: :razz: 

Screenshot ng Dreamweaver 8

### Post by lutosdemayo on 2006-01-05
[QUOTE=jeffreyvergara.NET]sensya na lutosdemayo hindi ako makasunod sa networking ng ubuntu. Y_Y

To logon to webmin kailangan gumagana din yung apache web server mo. Type mo sa firefox: [https://computer_name:10000/](https://computer_name:10000/). Yung computer_name yan ung pinangalan mo sa pc mo nung pag setup mo ng ubuntu. Hope this helps.

### Post by geonetrinity on 2006-01-06
@jeff 

Eto forum sa SSH
[http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=112331&highlight=Ssh+setup]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=112331&highlight=Ssh+setup")

Ok, nagwork na nga!!!

kapag nasa ibang computer ka, ang bina-browse mong computer sa terminal di na yung unit mo, yung host na nagconnect ka. 

ipabasa mo sa mga kaibigan mo kung mababasa nila, pagpumasok okey na yung computer mo... pwede ng mag SSH.

kapag makakapasok sila sa computer mo pwede na silang magsend ng files sa computer mo, at the same time pwede rin silang kumuha yun ang risk. Sa FTP my folder lang na pwede kang ishare, di ko alam kung pwede rin sa SSH.

Kasi SSH pag may pumasok na client, basa nya lahat ng files mo (pati hidden) kahit nasa root.

### Post by geonetrinity on 2006-01-06
X11 folder ...

Router kasi gamit ko meron pa akong dapat iconsider, para maaccess ko externally.

1. set up the router to forward port 22 requests to this computer.

2. then access from the Internet using the external router IP address.

Mas madali kung direct connection ako sa modem. 

Naalala ko dun sa streetfighter online di ako pwedeng mag host kasi router gamit ko, pwede lang mag host yung direkta sa modem.

sana mag work!!!

### Post by geonetrinity on 2006-01-12
Webcam Drivers

Mga tol you'll be needing this to run your webcam.

PLEASE FOLLOW ALL THE STEPS! BAWAL ANG SHORTCUTs IF YOU DONT KNOW WHAT YOU ARE DOING

You need to do the following from terminal:

sudo apt-get install linux-headers-`uname -r` linux-restricted-modules-`uname -r` build-essential gcc-3.4
wget [http://mxhaard.free.fr/spca50x/Download/spca5xx-20060101.tar.gz](http://mxhaard.free.fr/spca50x/Download/spca5xx-20060101.tar.gz)
tar xvfz spca5xx-20060101.tar.gz
cd spca5xx-20060101
sudo make CC=gcc-3.4
sudo modprobe -r spca5xx
sudo rm -rf /lib/modules/`uname -r`/kernel/drivers/usb/media/spca5xx*
sudo make install
sudo modprobe spca5xx

a4tech webcam ko working A-OK.

enjoy...

---

### Post by lx638 on 2006-01-12
[QUOTE=lutosdemayo]pre na try mo bang i download ung debian package ng yahoo as suggested by jsgotangco? baka di mo na install follow up ko lang kasi ung yahoo debian package na un talagang working sa breezy and you cannot just double click it and expect it to runs like windows. Curiosity ko lang at no offense taken, nakapag install ka na ba ng  *.deb na package?[/QUOTE]
bro natry ko na po pala un, sensya di ko nasabi. nabasa ko kasi sa isang thread:

[http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=81895](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=81895) 

1. Install libssl0.9.6 through Synaptic or sudo apt-get install libssl0.9.6

(prob ko, libssl0.9.7 ung nasa akin, kaya error)

2. Download this file from messenger.yahoo.com.(di ko na nilagay link pero un ung tinutukoy mo)

3. In a terminal, write:sudo dpkg -i /path/ymessenger_1.0.4_1_i386.deb
replacing path with the path to where you downloaded the file

(dito na nga lumabas ung mga errors)

4. Run /usr/bin/ymessenger and follow the few simple instructions for setting up Yahoo! Messenger. An icon will be placed on your desktop.

(ito di ko na nagawa)

wala pa akong experience sa linux kaya ganito pa ako katanga.hekhekhek ok lng yan no offense taken. gusto ko lng matuto.:D:D:D

### Post by geonetrinity on 2006-01-13
[http://lxer.com/module/newswire/view/51589/]("http://lxer.com/module/newswire/view/51589/")

Does the DoJ Use Microsoft as a Shill Against Linux?
Posted by tadelste on Jan 10, 2006 5:35 PM
LXer.com; By Tom Adelstein 	Mail this story
Print this story

Have fears of a resurgence of communism led the DoJ to suspect GNU/Linux communities of having anti-capitalistic agendas? If so, have they allowed Microsoft to engage in anti-trust to stop Free Software?

Have you ever chronicled the US Government's efforts to litigate Microsoft? When you step back and take a look, it seems as though the Department of Justice shopped around for a friendly judge and finally got one. You might even consider that we had two presidents with conflicts of interest with Microsoft and their own cabinets.

Why is this important? Because Microsoft has attacked and continues to attack GNU/Linux, the Free Software Foundation and a host of projects related to open source software. With Microsoft's considerable resources, they have mounted an ambitious campaign unlike any they have undertaken in the past. They intend to wipe us from the map.
Here's the progression:

    * DoJ performs massive investigation and enters into a decree->
    * Judge Sporkin refuses to approve->
    * DoJ/Microsoft joint appeal->
    * Judge Jackson hears case and rules to break up Microsoft->
    * Microsoft appeals->
    * Bush DoJ and Microsoft reach settlement->
    * Collen Kollar-Kotelly approves->
    * Microsoft goes back to business and attacks GNU/Linux.

How did this happen? Like I wrote above, Microsoft and their partner, the Department of Justice shopped for a friendly judge until they found one. It starts with a DoJ investigation headed up by Anne Bingaman. Most people believe in the spring of 1994 that she would file a major suite against Microsoft. But, after Bill Gates visit to the White House all that changed.
Failed Decree

The DoJ reached a settlement with Microsoft and took it to the first Judge Stanley Sporkin. In a memorandum opinion on Valentine's Day 1995, he launched into Microsoft wondering why the DoJ had made nothing of Microsoft's anti-trust case. Ultimately, Sporkin refused to approve the agreement and Microsoft and the DoJ appealed the decision. That's correct Microsoft and Justice, titular adversaries, filed a joint appeal.

The following June, a federal appeals court overturned Judge Sporkin and assigned the case to a different judge, Thomas Penfield Jackson.
Bill Gates Visits China

Bill Gates soon thereafter visited China where, after meetings with Jiang Zemin, Windows was declared the official operating system of the People's Republic of China. At just about the time of Gates's visit, the government of China began putting money into the Democratic Party's coffers. Conspiracy theorists find the chain of incidents strange. They consider it an unusual coincidence.
Anti-Trust Trial

We all know what happened next. The DoJ began a trial with Judge Jackson presiding. They called the filing, UNITED STATES OF AMERICA, Plaintiff, v. MICROSOFT CORPORATION, Defendant. With an embattled President going through impeachment, Microsoft started making new friends.
Enter the Republicans

From 1998-99, Jack Abramoff received $560,000 to lobby on behalf of Microsoft. Abramoff's associate, Ralph Reed received a $240,000 annual retainer while serving as a senior consultant to the Bush Campaign 2000. Reed's company's internal documents showed that his mission involved identifying and recruiting prominent Bush supporters to personally write and lobby Bush to back Microsoft.

Reed's contract with Microsoft came to the public's attention and proved an embarrassment to the Bush campaign in the summer of 2000. While under prosecution for anti-trust, Microsoft had hired a number of Bush aides as consultants and lobbyists. But nothing came of it.

Soon after Bush's inauguration, an appeals court overturned Judge Jackson's break-up order and the new DoJ got a new judge, Colleen Kollar-Kotelly. She approved what amounted to slap on the hand.
Ralph Nader the prophet

Lots of people thought Microsoft got off too easy and "the fix was in".

Ralph Nader wrote a letter to the court that you may consider prophetic. Let's take a look some of his points. He wrote (excerpts):

        * We note at the outset that the decision to push for a rapid negotiation appears to have placed the Department of Justice at a disadvantage.

        * We are disappointed of course to see a move away from a structural remedy (the break-up).

        * A need to have broader disclosure of file formats for popular office productivity and multimedia applications (exists).

        * Moreover, the agreement appears to give Microsoft too many opportunities to undermine the free software movement.

Microsoft Attacks Free Software

Nader may not have won the race to become President of the US, but he saw the future. Microsoft kept its file formats a secret, went after Peter Quinn and then opened the wrapper of its MSXML format. Of course, it's not really open since the specification requires anyone who uses it to include old undocumented proprietary formats such a WordML and RTF.

Microsoft has plenty of opportunities to undermine the free software movement. Microsoft has established a slush fund of $180 million to stop Linux from gaining government adoption anywhere on the globe. They have also put forth an unprecedented lobbying effort, have brought legal action against Brazil's head of IT, funded bogus benchmarks and TCO studies while restricting others from doing the same.

They have also set up shop on Linux news sites and spent untold amounts of money on their "Get the Facts" campaign. Take a look at Figure 1 and 2 and ask yourself if Microsoft's advertising seems appropriate for a convicted monopolist.

Where's the Anti-Trust Cops When You Need Them

Governments around the world have found Microsoft guilty of Anti-Trust as if that was a stretch. What does the Bush Administration do? Our Justice Department tells South Korea's Fair Trade Commission that they went too far in an antitrust judgment against Microsoft.

Last month, I spoke to Bob Price, former CEO of Control Data Corporation and author of The Eye for Innovation. We discussed a private anti-trust suit Control Data initiated against IBM back in 1968, when IBM was the nastiest monopoly in the world. Bob recalled the problems he had with the Department of Justice bringing any action against IBM.

As we spoke, I asked a series of questions about how dirty IBM behaved at the time of the CDC suit. My questions went something like this: Did IBM ever sue a public official in another country for wanting to use a different platform? Did IBM ever call a competitor a cancer? How far did they go in influencing members of Congress, the Judiciary, state representatives?

When I finished, Bob seemed astonished. He didn't know Microsoft was that insidious. As our discussion ended, I realized that the difference between CDC then and Linux now had to do with money. CDC could afford a legal action where it received a substantial settlement. The Linux people don't have those kinds of resources.

What we do need is a government that will take care of the people in this country and enforce the laws. What laws? Primarily the Sherman and Clayton anti-trust laws against Microsoft.

---

### Post by geonetrinity on 2006-01-13
Microsoft wins final FAT battle
Anne Broache
CNET News.com
January 11, 2006, 15:35 GMT
	
	
Two patents covering one of Microsoft's main Windows file-storage systems are valid after all, US federal patent examiners have decided.

The decision, announced Tuesday by the software giant, effectively ends a two-year saga over the patents and reverses two non-final rulings — the latest issued in October — in which the US Patent and Trademark Office rejected Microsoft's claims.

In their latest action, filed last week, the examiners concluded that the company's File Allocation Table (FAT) file system is, in fact, "novel and non-obvious", entitling it to patentability. Now the office is in the process of issuing a "patent re-examination certificate", which signals the finality of the decision, a Microsoft representative said.

The FAT file system, a common means of storing files, was originally developed for DOS, but has also been employed in Microsoft's Windows and on removable flash memory cards used in digital cameras and other devices. Some Linux- and Unix-related products also use the system to exchange data with Windows.

The Patent Office agreed to re-examine two patents covering the FAT system at the request of a little-known public interest group called the Public Patent Foundation in April 2004.

That organisation claimed there was "prior art" that proved Microsoft was not the first company to come up with the file format.

It also voiced concern that Microsoft would try to seek royalties from companies that sell and support Linux for using the technology, potentially posing a threat to the free software community. Under the terms of the GPL, Linux cannot be distributed if it contains patented technology that requires royalty payments.

Microsoft indicated in the past that it would license the file format. In December 2003, it said it had struck such a deal with flash memory vendor Lexar Media.

The Patent Office's final decision followed several non-binding decisions that were unfavourable to Microsoft. After issuing its preliminary rejection of the patents in September 2004, examiners handed down a similar decision about a year later.

All along, Microsoft voiced confidence that the patents would be upheld. David Kaefer, the company's director of business development, said Tuesday that the company was "very pleased" with the office's final decision. "This result underscores the validity of these patents but also the importance of allowing third parties to request re-examinations," he said in a statement.

Public Patent Foundation President Dan Ravicher said his organisation disagreed with the Patent Office's conclusions and offered a broader critique.

"Microsoft has won a debate where they were the only party allowed to speak, in that the patent re-examination process bars the public from rebutting arguments made by Microsoft," he told ZDNet UK sister site CNET News.com. "We still believe these patents are invalid and that a process that gave the public equal time to present its positions would result in them being found as such."
_______________________
Maraming complex effect ito, kapag nag push through yung case!!!

### Post by pinoyskull on 2006-01-13
@lx638
try mo reinstall yung dependencies

```

sudo apt-get remove <package name>

```

tapos install mo ulit sya
```

sudo apt-get install <package name>

```

### Post by lutosdemayo on 2006-01-13
[QUOTE=lx638]heto po ung errors:



ano po pwede gawin dito?[/QUOTE]

go to synaptic first and enable all of the repositories
Synaptic  >> Settings>Repositories 
at check mo lahat 
tapos click mo ung reload para ma refresh mo ung repositories
you can just search for the missing dependencies and install them thro synaptic or use  your gnome terminal and type this.

sudo apt-get install libgdk-pixbuf2
sudo apt-get install libgtk1.2
sudo apt-get install libssl0.9.6

or just

sudo apt-get install libgdk-pixbuf2 libgtk1.2 libssl0.9.6 

then try to re install the yahoo messenger 

i think that is all!!!! Gud luck!!!! ;) ;)

### Post by geonetrinity on 2006-01-20
Linux Users May be Violating Sarbanes-Oxley
By IT Observer Staff
Wednesday, 18 January 2006 17:35 EST

Companies using Linux for embedded applications may be unwittingly violating the Linux license and even breaking federal securities laws, according to a research published by Wasabi Systems.

The research “When GPL Violations are Sarbanes-Oxley Violations” is the first in a series of legal studies analyzing the common misperceptions and risks associated with Linux and its license, the GNU General Public License (GPL).

According to the study, the problem lies with the requirements of the Sarbanes-Oxley Act that companies disclose ownership of intellectual property to their shareholders. The study indicates that dozens of companies are discovered each year to have violated the terms of GPL, and if they are public companies, they are violating Sarbanes-Oxley.

“Linux is a powerful operating system,” says Jay Michaelson, an author of the study and Wasabi Systems’ General Counsel. “But if companies violate the license, the consequences can be more severe than they think. If companies are violating the GPL, they don’t have the right to use that software. And if they don’t have the right to use the software, they’re violating federal law if they claim that they do.”

The extent of this problem remains unclear. The Free Software Foundation, which is the primary enforcer of the GPL, reports that it pursues “several dozen” enforcement actions each year. In the past, such violators were merely required to release their code to the public. Now, Michaelson says, “Sarbanes changes the picture completely. For public companies, violating the Linux license is now a matter of federal securities law.”

Future studies will look at the GPL implications of Loadable Kernel Modules (LKM) and how upstream GPL violations impact VARs and end users.

### Post by andrija1989 on 2006-01-30
hi all..
ok what comands do i need to know for ubuntu.. since i am now to the while linux system i was just wondering what command do i have to type in the comand line... to get the proogram and does it have to be a specific of a program (mozilla firefox) or just like a random search liek antivirus or something..

---

### Post by lutosdemayo on 2006-01-30
[QUOTE=andrija1989]hi all..
ok what comands do i need to know for ubuntu.. since i am now to the while linux system i was just wondering what command do i have to type in the comand line... to get the proogram and does it have to be a specific of a program (mozilla firefox) or just like a random search liek antivirus or something..[/QUOTE]

Specify mo muna kung ano gagawin mo sa command line. If you want to updade you have to type sudo apt-get update. To delete files use rm filename. Ang daming linux commands available sa net.

Try this links:
[http://www.computerhope.com/unix.htm](http://www.computerhope.com/unix.htm)
[http://www.ss64.com/bash/](http://www.ss64.com/bash/)
[http://www.linuxdevcenter.com/linux/cmd/](http://www.linuxdevcenter.com/linux/cmd/)
[http://www.unixguide.net/linux/linuxshortcuts.shtml](http://www.unixguide.net/linux/linuxshortcuts.shtml)
[http://www.er.uqam.ca/nobel/r10735/unixcomm.html](http://www.er.uqam.ca/nobel/r10735/unixcomm.html)

That will get you started. pag gusto mo ng firefox type mo lang firefox tatakbo na ung firefox mo. Kung nag install ka ng program with in your own directory type mo lang ung /path/program.

### Post by geonetrinity on 2006-02-04
Loell:
I've had a tragic expirience with Ubuntulite 1.1, it wiped out all my files that ive been keeping for 12 months...   
_____________

Paano nawala yung files mo, wiped out ba yung partition o di mo lang ma access.


Nangyari na sa akin yan, di ko ma access yung partition at di ko makita sa filesystem.

(you can try this)
eto ginawa ko, gumamit ako ng live CD, 

1. pag ubuntu LIVE CD gagamitin mo magma mount ka pa sa terminal ng temporary folder.

2. SLAX live CD ng KDE(5.0.6 lang ok na), no mounting needing makikita mo na yung mga existing partition.

by then  pag nakita mo yung files mo, just reformat your system or transfer it using another hardisk kayang basahin ng SLAX yun. Pwede mo ring iburn using K3b ng SLAX.

Nung masira yung system ng ubuntu ko, di ko makita yung mga partition table, ganun lang ginawa ko.

---

### Post by loell on 2006-02-04
[QUOTE=geonetrinity]

(you can try this)
eto ginawa ko, gumamit ako ng live CD, 

1. pag ubuntu LIVE CD gagamitin mo magma mount ka pa sa terminal ng temporary folder.

2. SLAX live CD ng KDE(5.0.6 lang ok na), no mounting needing makikita mo na yung mga existing partition.

by then  pag nakita mo yung files mo, just reformat your system or transfer it using another hardisk kayang basahin ng SLAX yun. Pwede mo ring iburn using K3b ng SLAX.

Nung masira yung system ng ubuntu ko, di ko makita yung mga partition table, ganun lang ginawa ko.[/QUOTE]

I looked at the partitions already after it happend, using elive.. but it only confirmed what i've suspected. anyway i kinda accepted this incident, ano pa bang magagawa ko ;) ..   sabi nga nila, what doesn't kill you will only make you stronger.. lol... :-D

### Post by jsgotangco on 2006-02-07
Not in the morning session - its mostly business people like system builders, ISVs, training schools and such. It is after all a business meeting speaheaded by Canonical Ltd. and not the Ubuntu foundation.

We had a quick lunch (we talked mostly about what to expect in Seoul, Korea since I went there last year for a speaking engagement) the went to the NCC in Quezon City.

Mark then met with CICT officials. He gave a short speech to those who attended (mostly government people). The Bayanihan Linux team was also present. We ended the NCC session around 4pm and Mark went back to the hotel and flew for Tokyo around 6pm.

As for what the government (through the CICT, etc.) plans to do next is up to them really. Ubuntu is very well known in the Philippines now and with Mark arrving and speaking, things are looking bright.

Mark hinted he might comeback, although silently, to enjoy the view \\:D/ 

As for us, we're currently planning a community FOSS conference in August that is scheduled tentatively at the College of Saint Benilde (they are big users of Ubuntu - 2 labs worth of ubuntu installations!). We've already invited Richard Stallman and he said he'll come anytime. I talked to Mark about this and he's interested to come. Once we fix up the details, I'll be sending the invitation to his secretary.

### Post by jdash1 on 2006-02-09
mga tol help give some opinions about my problem in connecting dial up to my ubuntu linux...

i already have the modem driver..and capable ung internal modem ko na mag run sa linux....

the problem is medjo nalilito lng ako sa loob ng linux khit simple instructions ng manual a bit confused pa ako....help namn on this....




Installation
============

1. Unpack tar.gz package file:

	$ gzip -dc slmodem-2.9.X.tar.gz | tar xf -

2. 'cd' to package directory:

	$ cd slmodem-2.9.X

3. Review and edit 'Makefile' (if need):

   In many cases you will need to correct path to your local kernel
   source tree:

        KERNEL_DIR=/path/to/linux

   Default KERNEL_DIR is '/lib/modules/<kerne-version>/build'. Many Linux
   Distributions use directory '/usr/src/linux-<version>' also.

   Note: If you are using Linux kernel 2.4, only header files should be
         available for build in $(KERNEL_DIR)/include

   Another way to pass right value KERNEL_DIR is to use command line
   parameter while running 'make':

        $ make KERNEL_DIR=/path/to/linux ...

4. Run 'make' command to compile package:

	$ make

5. Install. As 'root' user run:

	# make install

   It will install:

   - application 'slmodemd' under '/usr/sbin' directory

   - hardware specific drivers (kernel modules) 'slamr' and 'slusb'
     under conventional kernel modules directory

   - character device nodes '/dev/slamr0-3' with major number 212
     (for pci modems) and '/dev/slusb0-3' with major number 213
     (for usb modems).

   - config modules for autoloading (by editing file '/etc/modules.conf')
     (only with 2.4 kernels)

6. Config modem country.

   Use AT+GCI=<T.35 country code> command to setup country.

   Also you can setup default modem country by passing command line
   parameter '--country=MY_COUNTRY' to program 'slmodemd'.

   See output of 'slmodemd --countrylist' for a list of supported
   country names and T.35 country codes (see also 'slmodemd --help').

   Note: Command ATI7 shows currently installed country setting.

8. Uninstallation.

   In package directory just type:

	# make uninstall


Getting Started
===============

After successful installation and configuration:

1. Load modem driver.

   Load your modem hardware specific kernel module:

	# modprobe slamr

   if you are using AMR/CNR/PCI modem, or

	# modprobe slusb

   if you are using SmartUSB56 Modem.

   Note: this will be done automatically when modules were
         configured for 'loading on demand'

   Note: this is safe to load both 'alamr' and 'slusb' modules.

2. Run soft modem application.

       # /usr/sbin/slmodemd [options] <device_name>

   Where device name is appropriate device node for your modem
   (look at output of 'dmesg' command).
   Run '/usr/sbin/slmodemd --help' for details.

   Examples:

       # /usr/sbin/slmodemd --country=USA /dev/slamr0

   , or for SmartUSB56 Modems:

       # /usr/sbin/slmodemd --country=ITALY /dev/slusb0

3. Using the modem.

   When 'slmodemd' is running this creates PTY (pseudo-terminal) to
   emulate modem port device, also this creates symbolic link
   like '/dev/ttySL0' (shown at startup).

   Config your application to use this link '/dev/ttySL0' (or PTY node
   itself) as modem port.

   Note: Some application want 'to know' that they are working with
         pseudo-terminal and may require additional configurations.

   Known application notes:

   - 'wvdial' requires option 'Carrier Check = no' in config file

   - some versions of 'kppp' may not work properly with devices named
     like '/dev/ttySL0'. To workaround this you may create symbolic link
     '/dev/modem' ( # ln -s /dev/ttySL0 /dev/modem ) and use this link
     as modem device with 'kppp'

4. Startup automation.

    There are examples of startup scripts in 'scripts' directory.




YAn kc ung Readme file n nabasa ko sa driver ng modem....my kylangan k p pla i set sa terminal....hinde ko alm kc ako kung alin sa 2 ung tamang lugar na pag installan ko.... 
ung...
1./lib/modules/<kerne-version>/build'
2./usr/src/linux-<version>

 KERNEL_DIR=/path/to/linux  <---hinde ko kc alam equivalent nito sa windows at saan ung location nito ?....(e2 ba ung C:/windows ?)

di ba pagbagong install mo ng ubuntu kylangan ba baguhin ung repositories...gamit ung "gedit" lng ?

### Post by berniej on 2006-02-19
I *was* able to dual boot OS X and Ubuntu Linux yesterday.  But I overlooked my OS X installation and I inadvertedly installed OS X 10.2.3 (Jaguar) instead of OS X 10.3.4 (Panther).  Anyway, after installing Jaguar (which took me around 2 hours since my hardware is pretty old -- a 300 MHz Clamshell iBook with 288 MB RAM, I installed Ubuntu "breezy" and i was successful in making it dual boot.

Kaso kumati ang kamay ko and I attempted to upgrade Jaguar to Panther and that's when my problems started.  The upgrade messed up the boot record and gave the boot-up control over back to OS X.  Since Panther took so long to install, I opted to abort the installation.  Since I can no longer boot in Ubuntu, I reinstalled it (no problems yet since I have not really started to use Ubunu).

To make the long story short -- I'm back to an Ubuntu-only installation on my Clamshell.  I'll try to play around with it more and when I have the time, I'll try to do a dual boot again later in the week.

### Post by jsgotangco on 2006-02-26
[QUOTE=jeffreyvergara.NET]pwede ba mag boot from .iso lang ng Live cd?[/QUOTE]

Depends on how you execute this. If you have a big USB disk, you can make it bootable and add the iso to be able to boot from USB. If you're doing it from the network, you have to create a dhcpd server and point to a tftpd server that has the iso. If from the hard drive, you may have to edit up GRUB to point to a bootable filesystem and have the iso reside there. You can read the installation guide in the CD for specific instructions on how to do this.

---

### Post by jeffreyvergara.NET on 2006-02-26
[QUOTE=jsgotangco] If from the hard drive, you may have to edit up GRUB to point to a bootable filesystem and have the iso reside there. [/QUOTE]

exactly! thanks jsgotangco!

hassle kasi pag insert ka pa ng CD everytime you want to try the live cd.

### Post by jsgotangco on 2006-03-15
huh? what do you mean exactly? The current milestone is *very* solid. The delay is meant for: QA, Hardware certification (laptop mission for example), OEM. The biggest changes that would happen are for input methods like SCIM, improving CJK support. The CJK issues came out after the Asian Tour and there is currently an l10n sprint to address it. Other teams will have extended freeze dates but will definitely not use whole 6 weeks, meaning the delay for 6 weeks is the maximum allowed time and could be shorter.

Of course, respecting freeze dates, app X (name your pick) will not go in dapper. There would be a change for version, but that is yet to be finalized.

Long time no POST!!! 

Dominic you can also try Mono para sa (.net)

What is Mono?

Mono provides the necessary software to develop and run .NET client and server applications on Linux, Solaris, Mac OS X, Windows, and Unix. Sponsored by Novell ([http://www.novell.com)](http://www.novell.com)), the Mono open source project has an active and enthusiastic contributing community and is positioned to become the leading choice for development of Linux applications. 

Info about mono:
[http://www.mono-project.com/Main_Page]("http://www.mono-project.com/Main_Page")
[http://www.mono-project.com/FAQ:_General]("http://www.mono-project.com/FAQ:_General")

These are some of the screenshots:
[http://www.mono-project.com/Screenshots]("http://www.mono-project.com/Screenshots")

If you are using UBUNTU, mono is easy to get:
(set your sources first)

sudo apt-get install mono
or
[http://www.mono-project.com/Downloads]("http://www.mono-project.com/Downloads")

(that's it)

**[COLOR="Blue"]Software developed with Mono[/COLOR]**

F-Spot photo management program
Enlarge
F-Spot photo management program
Muine music player
Enlarge
Muine music player

The following are programs that use the Mono API and C#.

    * Banshee is a music management and playback software for GNOME
    * Beagle is a desktop search tool.
    * Blam! is a RSS-news aggregator especially good for reading planet-feeds like Planet Gnome.
    * Bless is a hex editor.
    * CDCollect is a CD catalog application.
    * Diva is a video editing application for GNOME.
# F-Spot is a convenient photo management program developed by Novell.
# Galaxium is a MSN instant messenger (IM) client.
# GLyrics is a lyrics finder.
# Gpremacy is an implementation of the board game Supremacy written in Mono/Gtk#.
# iFolder 3 (by Novell) lets you share files across multiple computers and with other users through peer-to-peer or Novell's groupware server products.
# imeem a social networking software. Mac client and servers run Mono while the Windows client uses Microsoft.NET.
# MindFire is a cross-platform ebook reader designed to facilitate speed reading.
# MonoDevelop is an IDE for creating Mono applications. It was originally a port of SharpDevelop to Gtk#, but is today developed on its own. It is not currently available for Windows.
# Muine is a music player with a user interface designed to be intuitive, developed by Jorn Baayen who also worked on Rhythmbox.
# Second Life, the virtual world created by Linden Lab, will begin (1st Quarter 2006) compiling all of the scripts in their own Linden Scripting Language (LSL) to CIL. They will use an embedded Mono runtime to execute the CIL.
# SkyNET is a sky chart application.
# smuxi is an IRC client for advanced users written with Gtk#/Gnome#, SmartIrc4net and Nini.
# Tomboy is a desktop note-taking application which uses a wiki-like linking system.
# Virtuoso Universal Server, from OpenLink Software, is a cross-platform hosting environment for Mono/.NET/C#, JSP, Perl, Python, PHP, and other runtime environments. (Virtuoso is commercial software, starting at $5000)
___________________________

2005-06-27 02:38 - Anjuta C/C++ IDE
We are pleased to announce the release of Anjuta 2.0.1, the second development release of Anjuta DevStudio 2.x series.

This is an alpha & unstable release and may not be suitable for production use. However, we encourage to use it and help us with bug reports. Both stable and development release can be used simultaneously, but they should be installed in different install prefix (important).

### Post by geonetrinity on 2006-04-13
***[COLOR="Blue"]Eclipse [/COLOR]***

Eclipse is a free software / open source platform-independent software framework for delivering what the project calls "rich-client applications", as opposed to "thin client" browser-based applications. So far this framework has typically been used to develop IDEs (Integrated Development Environments), such as the highly-regarded Java IDE called Java Development Toolkit (JDT) and compiler that comes as part of Eclipse (and which are also used to develop Eclipse itself). However, it can be used for other types of client application as well. See the popular BitTorrent client Azureus for example.

Eclipse was originally developed by IBM as the successor of its VisualAge family of tools. Eclipse is now managed by the Eclipse Foundation, an independent not-for-profit consortium of software industry vendors. Many notable software tool vendors have embraced Eclipse as a future framework for their IDEs, among them Borland and IBM Rational.

kung medyo sinisipag kang mag download **[COLOR="Red"]NETBEANS[/COLOR]** can be installed on Ubuntu. (but you should be using high end computer 2.4 Mhz (with 768mb RAM) sa aking may kabagalan pa rin.
(netbeans location : [http://java.sun.com/j2se/1.4.2/download.html]("http://java.sun.com/j2se/1.4.2/download.html"))

Home Page:
[http://www.eclipse.org/]("http://www.eclipse.org/")
or
sudo apt-get install eclipse

Bayanihan  	

The first beta of the all-new Bayanihan Linux 4, now based on Debian 'sarge', has been released: "Bayanihan Linux 4 Beta 1 is now available for download. Features: Debian-based; latest kernel; KDE 3.5.0; OpenOffice.org 2.0; more productivity tools; Internet ready; multimedia playback; CD/DVD burning capability; educational applications; image editing tools; improved support for removable devices (USB); easy to update and upgrade. Note: The beta release will only work on IDE based hard disks. The support for SATA and SCSI hard drives will be added in the final release of Bayanihan Linux 4." 

eto yung download link:

[[RIGHT]http://www.bayanihan.gov.ph/downloads/BayanihanLinux4-beta1.iso[/RIGHT]]("http://www.bayanihan.gov.ph/downloads/BayanihanLinux4-beta1.iso")

### Post by loell on 2006-05-16
[QUOTE=darqtanian]help help help teach me please[/QUOTE]

i think if i'm not mistaken, you can already run ragnarok by using cedega :)

as for your gyach enhanced installation

download  "Gyach-Enhanced-pYVoiceChat-1.0.7-1.i586.rpm"

in [http://www.phrozensmoke.com/projects/pyvoicechat/index.php](http://www.phrozensmoke.com/projects/pyvoicechat/index.php)

at the downloads section it will be downloaded in your desktop

then click the terminal icon, in the terminal .. type

    
    -->  cd Desktop



then type

     
    --->  sudo alien Gyach-Enhanced-pYVoiceChat-1.0.7-1.i586.rpm 

the file Gyach-Enhanced-pYVoiceChat-1.0.7-1.i586.rpm will be converted to Gyach-Enhanced-pYVoiceChat-1.0.7-1.i586.deb

Then type

  -->   sudo dpkg -i Gyach-Enhanced-pYVoiceChat-1.0.7-1.i586.deb

gyach will  be installed

finally type

--> gyach


note: this install instruction is base on my typical installation of gyach enhanced, there might be better way to install gyach enhanced :)

gyach enhanced is good if you have a supported webcam in ubuntu..
you could use gaim instead :) anyway, thats just my instruction... please visit #ubuntu-ph on irc for further help. :p

### Post by Jucato on 2006-05-16
What is your ADSL provider? PLDT myDSL ako (ung P999 lang :D) and installing was simple. I just type in the terminal:
```
sudo pppoeconf
```
I just accept the defaults and enter my username and password when it asks for it. Then I also choose to automatically connect on startup. That's just what I did. I don't know if it's really correct way to do it but it worked for me.

---

### Post by noelonline on 2006-05-16
Finally I was able to use my dsl connection, hehehe! I was wrong to say that ubuntu doesn't support DSL out of the box, IT DOES! Just use "sudo pppoeconf." :)

---

### Post by Jucato on 2006-05-17
@noelonline: Wow! Glad to hear it worked! :D Yan, pwede ka na mag-celebrate! \\:D/

@darqtanian: regarding R.O. on Linux, unfortunately, any MMOG that uses nProtect GameGuard (which is almost all of the local MMOGs) does not work with WINE. I think , there were some "hacks" that were made before in order for the RO client to bypass GameGuard. However, this hack is illegal, at least for pRO. If you really want to play RO and don't mind playing on a private server, then there's good news. Private RO servers don't use GG and so gumagana siya. But private servers are also illegal, but that area has been pretty much shady, anyway. :D

### Post by loell on 2006-05-17
[QUOTE=darqtanian]hey can i ask a question. y when i need to type my password, i cannot input any letters or numbers..??? why??
and when i log in as root, what is the command i should use. thanks po[/QUOTE]

actually you can input any letters or numbers, hindi lang ipanapikita :)

so in the terminal when your asked with a password just type the correct one even if its not visible and it will be accepted..

when your in the root, the commands are still the same, just omit the "sudo" command..

### Post by jeffreyvergara.NET on 2006-05-24

### Post by Jucato on 2006-05-25
Well, there is, I think a DVD ISO that you can download. I'm just not sure.

Regarding dependencies, there's an option in apt-get (as well as in Synaptic) that just downloads the package you want and the dependencies it needs without installing it, saving the .deb files in a directory like /var/apt. I'm not sure about the exact location. I'm not logged into Kubuntu right now. The advantage of this is that you can download the packages (plus the dependencies) once, possibly on a unit with faster internet connection, copy those files on a CD-R/RW or USB drive, and install it on your own system, without internet connection. by using apt-get, you're sure (to a certain extent) that dependencies are also downloaded.

You could also try out [http://packages.ubuntu.com](http://packages.ubuntu.com) for downloadable .deb files. Just check their dependencies as listed and download those as well.

---

### Post by jsgotangco on 2006-05-25

### Post by Jucato on 2006-05-28
It would help if you could tell us what you were trying to install from source, so that we could assist you if we had the experience in installing it.

Also, have you tried looking for the same program in the repositories? I usually follow this step by step procedure when looking for a certain app.

1. Look in the repositories: installing from the repos is the easiest, so why reinvent the wheel when you don't need to. You could try looking for the software in [http://packages.ubuntu.com](http://packages.ubuntu.com), to see if it's available in Ubuntu at all.

2. Look for .deb installers: some stuff from KDE-Apps or KDE-Look fortunately have .deb installers. If you're lucky, you might also find an Ubuntu-specific installer, too. Be careful, though, where you get the .deb files. We can't be too careful. :D

3. Lastly, the .tar.gz or source code: before you compile, make sure that you install the *build-essential* package, which will install everything that you need to compile stuff. Make sure you also follow instructions carefully, if they are available. Usually, you can find some instructions once you uncompress/extract the .tar.gz archive. Once you have uncompressed it, go to the directory where you extracted it and type (one after the other):
```
./configure
make
sudo make install
```
Of course, you have to wait for each process to finish before you type in the next command. 

Take note that not everything that comes in source code can always be compiled, especially if it requires libraries or packages that are not yet installed, or worse, shouldn't be installed yet (this happens with newer packages, sometimes).

This web page might also help: [http://www.psychocats.net/ubuntu/installingsoftware.php](http://www.psychocats.net/ubuntu/installingsoftware.php)
It has a lot of info on Ubuntu/Linux, so read up. ;D

Hope that helps a bit.

### Post by Jucato on 2006-06-01
Sa wakas!!!!
As of 11:15 PM
> ~$ lsb_release -a
No LSB modules are available.
Distributor ID: Ubuntu
Description:    Ubuntu 6.06 LTS
Release:        6.06
Codename:       dapper

But my upgrade has been anything but painful. Started updating at 9:30am, had a few dependency problems (205 packages to be uninstalled), and culminated with a X problem. So total of almost 14 hours!! Akala ko pa naman madali mag upgrade sa Linux. Anyway part of it was my fault, I guess. I had around 1000+ packages installed from a mixture of official Ubuntu packages and some installed through .deb or source.

Well, anyway, just a few tips for our kababayan from me:
1. Uninstall things that you absolutely don't need, or things that you could live without for the next few days. Less packages installed, less things to be updated, less download time.
2. Don't panic at once when Adept/Synaptic greets you with messages like "# packages to be removed". Take deep breaths and look at the packages/messages. Chances are, some of these things can be reinstalled later on. Just take note of what things are going to be removed. In my case, apt had to remove 205 packages in order to upgrade, most of them KDE/GUI stuff. So I went ahead and removed them, and reinstalled kubuntu-desktop so that they could be reinstalled again. (Salamat sa kubuntu-desktop metapackage!)
3. Find something to do to kill time while upgrading, lalo kung marami-rami. It's both exciting and nerve wrecking to see all those lines going up or those bars filling up. Maybe it's a nice time to catch up on your reading, or just watch TV. :D

Yun lang po. based lang sa personal experience ng first time upgrader.
Enjoy Dapper Drake! Enjoy being a duck! :p

### Post by digitalkarabao on 2006-06-08
mga tsong..tulong naman o...pinost ko na to sa general help at laptop support e, pero alang dumarating na tulong...hehe..

hassle lang kasi yung lm-sensors. installed yung lm-sensors pero pag ni-run ko na yung 'sensors' command, no sensors found!...

nag-sensors-detect ako nasa ibaba ang result...i was able to run the sensors fine previously on Breezy. nangyari lang to after upgrading to dapper.

root@digitalpenguin:/home/auric# sensors-detect
# sensors-detect revision 1.393 (2005/08/30 18:51:1

This program will help you determine which I2C/SMBus modules you need to
load to use lm_sensors most effectively. You need to have i2c and
lm_sensors installed before running this program.
Also, you need to be `root', or at least have access to the /dev/i2c-*
files, for most things.
If you have patched your kernel and have some drivers built in, you can
safely answer NO if asked to load some modules. In this case, things may
seem a bit confusing, but they will still work.

It is generally safe and recommended to accept the default answers to all
questions, unless you know what you're doing.

We can start with probing for (PCI) I2C or SMBus adapters.
You do not need any special privileges for this.
Do you want to probe now? (YES/no):
Probing for PCI bus adapters...
Use driver `i2c-sis96x' for device 00:02.1: Silicon Integrated Systems SMBus Controller
Probe succesfully concluded.

We will now try to load each adapter module in turn.
Module `i2c-sis96x' already loaded.
If you have undetectable or unsupported adapters, you can have them
scanned by manually loading the modules before running this script.

To continue, we need module `i2c-dev' to be loaded.
If it is built-in into your kernel, you can safely skip this.
i2c-dev is already loaded.

We are now going to do the adapter probings. Some adapters may hang halfway
through; we can't really help that. Also, some chips will be double detected;
we choose the one with the highest confidence value in that case.
If you found that the adapter hung after probing a certain address, you can
specify that address to remain unprobed. That often
includes address 0x69 (clock chip).

Next adapter: SiS96x SMBus adapter at 0x0c00
Do you want to scan it? (YES/no/selectively):
Client found at address 0x08
Client found at address 0x10
Client found at address 0x30
Client found at address 0x31
Client at address 0x50 can not be probed - unload all client drivers first!
Client at address 0x51 can not be probed - unload all client drivers first!

Some chips are also accessible through the ISA bus. ISA probes are
typically a bit more dangerous, as we have to write to I/O ports to do
this. This is usually safe though.

Either your sensors are not supported, or they are
connected to an I2C bus adapter that we do not support.
See doc/FAQ, doc/lm_sensors-FAQ.html, or
[http://www2.lm-sensors.nu/~lm78/cvs/...nsors-FAQ.html](http://www2.lm-sensors.nu/~lm78/cvs/...nsors-FAQ.html)
(FAQ #4.24.3) for further information.
If you find out what chips are on your board, see
[http://secure.netroedge.com/~lm78/newdrivers.html](http://secure.netroedge.com/~lm78/newdrivers.html) for driver status.

---

### Post by mumushi on 2006-06-22
ok kuya i already installed my lamp server using the ubuntu server disk. it really did not make me cry installing it my problem is when it booted up and got to the prompt i don't know what's next. i'm stranded.. dunno where to go. dunno the commands... i wanted to set up my web server.. that's my main objective. any howto or guide i could use? thank you so much for the help. muahhh!

---

### Post by jsgotangco on 2006-06-22
well yes it is a server and does not install any fancy desktop environment. What you would want to do is try using another computer and open up a web browser then go to the IP address of the server machine that you just made and the root directory of the server will show up.

There is a server guide available at [https://help.ubuntu.com/ubuntu/serverguide/C/index.html](https://help.ubuntu.com/ubuntu/serverguide/C/index.html) but this assumes you have practical console experience. If not refer to the desktop guide.

### Post by Jucato on 2006-06-26
Nautilus (Ubuntu/GNOME's file manager) has a built in CD burning utility, if all you need is to burn data to the CD. Press Ctrl+L (location bar) and type in burn:/ and you will be given an area where you can drag and drop files to be burned. Similar to Windows XP's built in Roxio burner.

---

### Post by Jucato on 2006-06-29
I also used Chikka's Javalite, but it needs Sun's Java, not the open source Java. While it's not really a very big deal, I only have 640 MB RAM. Even with many applications open, my system rarely needs to use the swap. But when running Sun's Java, the system is forced to use the swap memory. Like I said, it isn't really a big deal, but it slows things down a bit. 

And of course, if there was an alternative, one that would integrate very well with GAIM/Kopete, then why not use it. :D

although continuing the thread will be a good thing,
and i'm in favor with it by the way..

this thread has also a minor side effect on ubuntuforums
ie: when we post here and then the next minute someone in the other part of the world is searching  a keyword for a solution in ubuntuforums, and it so happen that the keyword is mentioned in this thread, the thread will actually be included in the top search results, where it should have been other threads with more relevance
on the search topic, can this become a little dilemma on continuing the thread?

1. Windows-only software for my Windows Smartphone 2002/HTC Tanager/QTek 7070/Orange SPV e100. I have tried running some of them in Wine with no luck.
2. When my sister is downloading something important, but I need to use the PC, I just switch over to my own user account
3. When I have to play some MMORPGs (which hasn't happened recently).

### Post by jeffreyvergara.NET on 2006-07-05
ganda setup ko ngaun ng system ko.. sa tingin ko lang ha.. ^^

Harddisk1
hda1 = /boot (100mb)
hda2 = /linux-swap (1gb)
hda3 = /root (10gb)
hda4 = /home (remaing space)

Harddisk 2 (boot manager installed here)
Windows XP Pro

kahit masira ngaun ubuntu ko, ok pa rin ang pag boot ng windows ko, and vice versa.. pwedeng changed ko nalang sa bios kung anong harddisk ang i-boot sa startup... hehehe

---

### Post by Jucato on 2006-07-05
ehehe! ganyan din halos setup ko. nasa ibang hard disk ang windows. Pero primary master ang windows, tapos ang GRUB sa floppy naka install, para hindi n kailangang istorbohin ang MBR ng Windows. Useless nga lang kung yung Desktop CD ang gagamitin mo pang install. :D

Btw, suggestion ko lang kuya, gumawa ka na po ng isang extended/logical partition, para hindi ka limited sa 4 partitions lang. Unless 100% absolutely sure ka na hindi ka mangangailangan ng iba pang partition.
