### Post by shinkaide on 2006-07-13
> **loell said:**
> tayo-tayo rin gagawa nang script if ever , maybe shinkaide can guide us or give us tips for that :D

that would a nice idea to put it in Ubuntu-PH website, yun ay kung ok lang kay kuya Jerome :)

Well... usually pag gumagawa ka ng comic script... first jot down the main idea and the setting of the story. Kahit sa scratch lang, scribble down what story ideas you have.

Then, if you want to really really refine it, Write the script for each panel. Include in short sentences what the characters do in a panel, and include their dialogue.

That's basically it for comic writing... some people just skip the script entirely and just start drawing with the idea in their heads.

Apir! :D

### Post by Jucato on 2006-07-13
also be prepared to talk about non-proprietary/open multimedia formats, because this is one aspect where Ubuntu stands out from the rest, which might also make it harder for most people to actually start using it in our local setting. Because of the rampart use and spread of MP3s and DivX videos, codecs would be a very strong factor influencing acceptance of Linux.

-------------------------------------------------------------------
Maiba ko lang po topic saglit...

I'm planning to buy a new mouse tomorrow, because my perfectly working PS/2 mouse (from CD-R King) is no longer supported by the latest Linux kernels (2.6.15-25 up to 2.6.17).

I need advice whether to buy a PS/2 or a USB mouse. Which one is/will be more supported in Linux/Ubuntu? And is Logitech a good brand, or is there something better?

Thanks po!!

### Post by shinkaide on 2006-07-13

-------------------------------------------------------------------

I'm planning to buy a new mouse tomorrow, because my perfectly working PS/2 mouse (from CD-R King) is no longer supported by the latest Linux kernels (2.6.15-25 up to 2.6.17).

I need advice whether to buy a PS/2 or a USB mouse. Which one is/will be more supported in Linux/Ubuntu? And is Logitech a good brand, or is there something better?

Thanks po!!

Yep, I agree; in this day and age codecs are very important. I had the initial frustration of not being able to play my mp3 collection and some videos, but quickly solved about 90% of my problems after tracking down the right packages in the Ubuntu Repository. (yeah, I didn't know about easybuntu until a few hours  after that). I still [have to resolve my VCD problems]("http://www.ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=213974"), but besides that, I'm great.

I take it that easybuntu solves majority of these problems. If so, new users shouldn't be scared off as much. Unless they're content creators with kung-fu grips on Photoshop and Flash, you should be able to convince them to switch, if all they need is Office and the regular multimedia playing stuff.

Logitech? Go for it dude; Best mice ever (IMHO; and Micro$oft a distant second). If you have USB ports to spare, go. If you can't spare one, go with the ps2. Most  linux distros support USB mice from the get-go now (used to be hard to set up with mandrake when I used it - had to tweak my bios to get it to work).

Apir! :-D

### Post by Jucato on 2006-07-17
Just bought a new mouse so that I could use Linux kernels above 2.6.15-23 (long story...). My old mouse was a PS/2 Optical Wheel Mouse from CD-R King, costing only Php 150. It's still working perfectly, but the Linux kernel will no longer support it starting version 2.6.15-25. Sucks... but I've got a new mouse. I bought this new Logitech USB Optical Wheel mouse for Php 600. And that was the cheapest one I could find. Or at least the cheapest mouse that I was sure would also work on Linux (forever??).

I just observed some things, though. I bought this at Festival Mall in Filinvest, Alabang, so my observations might not apply in other places.

1. Most sales personnel don't know what Linux is. The ones who probably do are the people in the back room doing some repairs. 

2. There are very few hardware/accessories that explicitly support Linux. Most of the time it's just Window/Mac or PC/Mac. The mouse I bought was for PC/Mac, but I just presumed that PC = Windows/Linux/Unix/BSD :D

3. There was only one shop (I think it was TCA, The Computer Authority) that had a display computer with Linux running. It was running Lindows. Placed beside Windows XP, the name easily looks/sound like a pirated Windows OS. Of course, with products like Sonya DVD players or Nokina cellphone accessories, it's too easy to jump to that conclusion. They also didn't "arrange" the desktop very well, so that the Lindows desktop actually looks a bit unattractive.

---

### Post by lixx on 2006-07-17
> **Fenyx said:**
> 
2. There are very few hardware/accessories that explicitly support Linux. Most of the time it's just Window/Mac or PC/Mac. The mouse I bought was for PC/Mac, but I just presumed that PC = Windows/Linux/Unix/BSD :D


Hmm. I dont agree with you. On my HP nx6120 laptop, i didn't encounter hardware problems. Intel 910 Mobile, Broadcom Netxtreme and Wireless, TI Card reader and the synaptics touchpad was detected and configured well without user intervention. The only thing that was undetected was the Agere Softmodem, but with the help of Smart Link's driver, I was able to dial-up in a breeze. There are many hardware/accessories that explicitly support Linux, but Linux isn't that common, so they just place Win or Mac.

### Post by Jucato on 2006-07-17
> **lixx said:**

The only thing that was undetected was the Agere Softmodem, but with the help of Smart Link's driver, I was able to dial-up in a breeze. There are many hardware/accessories that explicitly support Linux, but Linux isn't that common, so they just place Win or Mac.

What I meant by "explicit" is that the hardware/accessory has something written on the box that it supports Linux. When you bought those pieces of hardware, did the box have any markings that say out loud that it will work in Linux? Most of the time, it doesn't. There are a few, though, that do. But they are the exceptions rather than the rule.

### Post by Jucato on 2006-07-19

### Post by shinkaide on 2006-07-19
> **Fenyx said:**
> Mga kababayan, have you heard of this local web hosting service? [http://www.philhosting.net](http://www.philhosting.net)

Parang maganda eh. There are payment plans as low as Php 30/month. Sounds too good to be true... That's why I'm not so sure about it's authenticity/reliability. Pero if it is true... Php 30/month... :mrgreen:

EDIT: I just noticed, at the footer, it says CentOS. Does that mean it's running on CentOS? Too bad on the same line it also says MS FrontPage Support. :twisted:

Let me just say something about these guys: **Bad customer support**. They're not the worst, but they're not very good either.

I tried the P30 a month plan initially and was going good. Then, I upgraded my plan two times within a short span of time due to the increasing traffic that my site was getting. That's when the trouble started happening.

During that transitory period I was updating ESD heavily - 5 times a week. Now, involved in these upgrades was moving my account - account info, content (databases, files, etc.) - to different servers (as different plans mean different servers). It gets mucky here. 

During the first few days of the transition from the basic account to the higher accounts, I still kept on updating daily. This basically meant that when I updated and they moved my account, I lost one day of updates (since their site backups are one day old). Being very new (and thus very clueless) to paid webhosting (as I was used to Geocities, Tripod, etc.), I had no idea just what was going on. So I panicked naturally, and emailed tech support to try and know what was going on. 

They did not give me a clear explanation that would make it clear what was happening. They could have told me that *"this is expected, since we're moving your account to another server, you should perhaps refrain from updating during so-and-so days to avoid data loss"*. Unfortunately, this was not the case. Customer Support was inept enough to omit this useful bit of information that would have prevented me from further updating and thus bringing further frustrating myself, since I did not understand what was involved in the process.

You could say it's my fault for not knowing - partly, maybe - but the fact that this repeated itself more than once and CS failed to at least try to explain what I should and should not do/expect says a lot about them. Good customer support should do more than just write "don't worry sir, we'll fix it for you". They should consider the not only the technical problem at face value, but also the customer's situation and give the appropriate and useful response. They didn't do that.

In short I lost close to about a week's worth of data (including a laborous site overhaul), and I wasn't happy with their customer support. So I switched to bluehost, a US-based webhost that's gotten awards for customer support (and more). And upon calculation, their basic account gave me more bang for my back than some of the higher-tier hosting options PhilHosting gave me. I made the switch, I couldn't have been happier... for a few more months. Than Philhosting came back to bite me in my newbie ***.

When I switched, I failed to cancel my account, as per the Philhosting license agreement. Fair enough, my bad. So they continued to charge me every month even though no bandwidth at all was consumed, and they didn't even bother to email me *"sir, we find it anomalous that you're not consuming any bandwidth and that you have redirected your URL to a different nameserver. Have you moved? Should we cancel your account so that you won't be kept being charged for nothing?"*. Granted, they're obviously not legally obligated to do that, but it would have been very much appreciated if they did so. It became very apparent that shit would hit the fan as soon as I recieved a billing statement a few months later.

While I was happily coding away in my new host, Philhosting sent me a billing statement for a few months where I had not consumed any bandwidth. So I sent them an email saying that I wanted to cancel my account. When I did, they hijacked my domain name and told me until I paid them for the said months, I wouldn't be able to use it. Even though I didn't use any bandwidth from them.

According to their license agreement when I signed up for their hosting package, there was no provision included there that would let them legally hijack my domain and use it as a hostage should there be some problems with an account. So it would have been illegal under the old Terms of Service.

But they also had a provision that would let them change the TOS anytime and anyway they see fit. So they changed the TOS, and during the time I had this problem with them, they could legally screw me over like they did until I couged up the dough.

Very sneaky, eh? And apparently (recently) very legal too. 

In short, I paid up just to end the ordeal and didn't try to fight the moral injustice I was experiencing anymore, because I couldn't - thanks to the new TOS (I actually had a lawyer friend of mine examine the Old TOS which Philhosting sent me when I applied for the account and then the new TOS which was silently changed and posted on their website). Very suspiciously changed at quite a convenient time, I must add.

After that I dove into [_bluehost_]("http://www.bluehost.com")'s knowledge base to read up on relevant material and hope to fully secure everything critical to my site's function.

I know enough now not to make a fool of myself and not to get screwed over again.

Cheap prices can only keep a customer in for so long. I'd rather pay more for a host that really takes care of the customer and doesn't act like a cold, corporate entity. I will take good customer service over cheap prices anytime.

I'm not saying these are bad guys, but they aren't good. Sure, they host big philippine companies. But what about the little guys like us? Go with a US-based webhost. Better bang for the buck, and their basic hosting already kicks way more *** than most of Philhosting's basic to higher-tier hosting packages.

---

### Post by jsgotangco on 2006-07-27
Hi all,

Hope all is well in the community. At the moment, we have a revamped website ([www.ubuntu-ph.org](www.ubuntu-ph.org)) and starting to take shape with the help of some people.

I'm sending this email to present a proposal I've discussed with some people in the #ubuntu-ph channel on freenode IRC regarding the group and how to improve community involvement. So far I'm getting positive responses so I'm pushing this now via email.

As most of you know, I am based in Quezon City as well as some people visibly active in the community, but in my travels outside the city, I have met a lot of people using Ubuntu and organizing various activities in their own respective communities that even exceed those happening in the capital region.

So obviously, UBUNTU-PH != Greater Manila Area.

This is what I would like to cultivate and grow fruit in the future. I would like to see people active in their local community get the exposure from the global ubuntu community and eventually have people contribute to development of free software in general. Most people have the skills to make it possible; they just don't know where to start and having a tight local community can translate to a lot of things in unlocking the potential of people.

I'm proposing that we split UBUNTU-PH into three major subgroups:
Luzon, Visayas and Mindanao. It's possible to have minor subgroups within major subgroups (Like Ubuntu Zamboanga be under Ubuntu Mindanao) as Launchpad makes it possible. These major subgroups are distinct from each other, may organize their own activities, and have a representative get author access rights to the Ubuntu-ph.org website as well as add more people into Planet.

In turn, recognized ubuntu-members can act as mentors on guiding these groups/people on how to be more involved into development of Ubuntu itself with the goal of having more technical people involved in free software development and non-technical people involved in advocacy, artwork, marketing, etc.

We would like to make this community-based as much as possible. We may be affiliated with various organizations that may or may not have Ubuntu as part of their business strategy - that is fine as long as business interests do not get into the community itself.. What we would like to see is have a very healthy free software ecosystem based on Ubuntu with a very good community of users and supporters.

I'm also calling for an IRC meeting on August 1, 2006 at 8pm (+8UTC) in the #ubuntu-ph IRC channel on freenode so we could discuss more of this as a community. If an IRC meeting is not possible, we may also do a Y!M group chat for those not able to do via IRC.

Best,

Jerome G.

---

### Post by loell on 2006-08-31
@rabosajr , piliin mo lang ang mga compatible webcams na pwede sa ubuntu or linux in general, if the webcam is included in [spca5xx]("http://mxhaard.free.fr/spca5xx.html") base driver and says "yes" in support the column, then that webcam is good to go, just plug it in.. and you can use it.

### Post by Jucato on 2006-09-17
> **mostwanted said:**
> Many of you switch into English in midsentence and back to, well, I'm not sure what the language is called, but I'm sure it's the main Fillipino language :)

Are you aware that you do this? It's a funny thing to switch between languages like that ;)

1. It's not the main Filipino language. The main Filipino language is, well, Filipino (or Tagalog, depending on what you were taught at school). "Taglish" is a sort of corruption or a colloquial form of Filipino/English. It's not used in formal speech/conversations. Also, Filipino has more lenient rules when it comes to using English words in Filipino sentences where no suitable translation is available, specially for technical terms, like in "i-click mo yung OK sa dialog box".

2. It's funny from an outsider's point of view, but quite normal within the local setting. Except when there's a very "drastic" and abnormal shift in the sentence like in "it's so kadiri!" (conyo?).

---

### Post by mostwanted on 2006-09-17
> **Jucato said:**
> 1. It's not the main Filipino language. The main Filipino language is, well, Filipino (or Tagalog, depending on what you were taught at school). "Taglish" is a sort of corruption or a colloquial form of Filipino/English. It's not used in formal speech/conversations. Also, Filipino has more lenient rules when it comes to using English words in Filipino sentences where no suitable translation is available, specially for technical terms, like in "i-click mo yung OK sa dialog box".

I wasn't saying "Taglish" was the main language, I was saying you switch between English and the main language (which I was subsequently told was called Tagalog).

I speak a language which also lacks many modern technical terms (Danish), but we simply "Danify" English words and use them in Danish sentences. We never switch completely into English :)

### Post by hk_2999 on 2006-09-17
[QUOTE=erwinquita]Ei!

My smart bro connection used to work and I've been using for 2 months now... pero ngayon pag booth ko ng pc ko ayaw na gumana ng internet connection ko... di na ako makapag browse... have you encountered this problems too? as of now I'm booting in windows to search for a solution...

any help would be appreciated...

That happened to me too. I use Smart Bro. I'm planning to make a howto about that, but anyway, for lack of time, I'll just give you this link that helped me connect. 

[http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=186848]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=186848")
Also, be aware to copy IP settings from Windows and not the guy's IP. And transfer them to ubuntu's Network Settings. Including the DNS servers.

P.S. I'm using ubuntu to write this post right now, thanks to that article. I'm also planning to ditch Windows, not economical reasons or anything but because of Spyware, viruses, hackers and, slowdowns. :(

### Post by hk_2999 on 2006-09-17
[QUOTE=mostwanted]
Quote:
Originally Posted by Jucato View Post
1. It's not the main Filipino language. The main Filipino language is, well, Filipino (or Tagalog, depending on what you were taught at school). "Taglish" is a sort of corruption or a colloquial form of Filipino/English. It's not used in formal speech/conversations. Also, Filipino has more lenient rules when it comes to using English words in Filipino sentences where no suitable translation is available, specially for technical terms, like in "i-click mo yung OK sa dialog box".

I wasn't saying "Taglish" was the main language, I was saying you switch between English and the main language (which I was subsequently told was called Tagalog).

I speak a language which also lacks many modern technical terms (Danish), but we simply "Danify" English words and use them in Danish sentences. We never switch completely into English [/QUOTE]

*To Jucato: *Tol, pwede naman yung "i-click mo yung OK sa dialog box", "i-click mo yung Sige sa dialog box". Kaso nga lang, corny hehe.

*To mostwanted:* Actually, we do tagalogify our words. Computer becomes kompyuter, etc, and we have a set of rules to do that. Although, some words like juxtaposition or cyberspace, just cant have any other spelling.

But most of us guys are, I'm sorry to admit, just too lazy to abide to those rules, and some don't even remember them, as poverty has risen in our country so has the quality of education kind of decreased. A majority of our population don't even get the chance to go to college. :(

Also, I have heard on filipino class, there are many new rules our langguage organization made but they haven't reached the heart of the masses even until now. Another problem is Tagalog is just a virtual main langguage, some people I know in Cebu don't even know how to speak Tagalog. And as you can see, English had became a major language here because we were an American colony and there are many job offerings here that has good english skills as the most important factor - like call center jobs and outsourcing to other countries.

So that also explains why we use tag-lish. To practice english, and if sometimes run out of it, revert to well, Tagalog.

### Post by zek725 on 2006-11-01
Xubuntu Dapper to Xubuntu Edgy upgrade successful with problem with **courier-authdaemon ** which was resolved with a dirty fix [http://www.ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=285466&highlight=courier](http://www.ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=285466&highlight=courier). However, Firefox failed to upgrade to 2.0. For some reason it was even downgraded to 1.5.0.2!

I tried a clean install of Xubuntu Edgy Eft but halt no longer powers down the pc. [http://www.ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=1090643#post1090643](http://www.ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?p=1090643#post1090643) but was solved by adding **acpi=force lapic** to the kernel entry in /boot/grub/menu.lst :) Solb na! Kaya masaya na ako sa faster bootup in Edgy. :D

### Post by _duncan_ on 2007-01-17
puwedeng gawin sa firefox. i-click mo Edit > Preferences. Doon sa Main tab hanapin mo ang Startup Box. Doon may option na "When Firefox starts". Piliin mo ang "Show my windows and tabs from last time". Ayos na!

### Post by Jucato on 2007-02-13
It would have been nice if you could have contacted someone from the Ubuntu Philippines LoCo team regarding this. The current forums is a bit limited in content and features, but mostly because there has been no apparent "demand" for services. Kakaunti nga lang tayo, hindi pa magkasama-sama. Sa ngayon, mahirap buuin ang Ubuntu-PH community, at napakahirap gumawa ng pagbabago sa site/forums... :(

As for the screencasts, I'm not sure if it's possible to embed those in the current ubuntu-ph forums, and I'm even less sure if some of the higher ups would even approve of providing such a feature. Some people might not like having Flash content enabled in the site, so I guess in this case, a spin-off site would be better. 

Anyway, here are the places where you can get in touch with the official Ubuntu Philippines Team:

Launchpad: [https://launchpad.net/~loco-philippine-team](https://launchpad.net/~loco-philippine-team)
IRC: #ubuntu-ph at irc.ubuntu.com or irc.freenode.net
Mailing List: [email]ubuntu-ph@lists.ubuntu.com[/email] ([https://lists.ubuntu.com/mailman/listinfo/ubuntu-ph](https://lists.ubuntu.com/mailman/listinfo/ubuntu-ph))
Website: [http://ubuntu-ph.org/](http://ubuntu-ph.org/)
Planet Ubuntu-PH: [http://ubuntu-ph.org/planet/](http://ubuntu-ph.org/planet/)
Ubuntuforums thread: this one :) [http://www.ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=68805](http://www.ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=68805)

This is a plea, actually a real loud and frustrated cry, for help. If you have ideas or suggestions or areas where you can help, please do contact us, or put them in here. I check the forums 4 times a day for updates, so I won't miss posts in this thread. 

Let's try to put some life into our LoCo. Kahit online collaboration naman siguro pwede, kasi mahirap ang actual, real life, meetings. Ika nga sa isang slogan "Buhayin ang Ubuntu-PH! Atin 'to!"

### Post by chimp_rex on 2007-08-04
I have tried Bayanihan Linux 3.1, 4.0beta, and 4.0 stable. It's very user-friendly...parang Windows XP or kaya Lindows ang dating.  Maraming nakasamang software...mostly for educational use. Maganda ang pagkagawa, GUI-wise, ng ASTI. Pero, primary concern ko kasi ang support. Dalawa lang ata ang sumasagot parati sa forums ng [www.bayanihan.gov.ph](www.bayanihan.gov.ph). Tuloy, I opted for Ubuntu...ganda ng support.

---

### Post by Jucato on 2007-08-04
I just recently installed Bayanihan Linux 4.0. I don't know how to react. On one hand almost everything went well. It's based on Debian Sarge (old...) but uses the Anaconda installer (from Red Hat), so that was a bit curious. However, the installer was sort of "stripped" down into very, very basic steps. I don't know why. The artwork looks good, I actually like the bootsplash screen and the splash screen. Of course it uses KDE, which is a plus for me.

The honeymoon stops when I tried to install nvidia-glx, as per the release notes. installing that tried to remove all xserver stuff. To make things a bit more difficult, I couldn't connect to any bayanihan.gov.ph site using the DNS from PLDT, so support was a bit difficult.

I'd have to agree with chimp_rex, support (and documentation) might be one of the biggest drawbacks of Bayanihan Linux. That and the actual need that Bayanihan tries to fill. For a government-affiliated project, it feels a bit underdeveloped (surprise, surprise?) and sort of "kalat". I don't know what Bayanihan aims to be/do, but right now I'm not seeing it.

Maybe it's a lack of interest... The Ubuntu-PH community (at least the older/elder ones) aren't really spectacular either... We haven't had any activity or meeting for half a year... :(

Buti na lang may international community to lean on. :P

---

### Post by bme on 2007-08-04
When I was "active" on the Bayanihan lists somebody in that lists made fun of me....a certain professor who was part of the Bayanihan team...I introduced myself as an OFW( I still am BTW)...People on that team had the nerve to ask for pasalubong whenever I get home(perhaps a joke?).
Then that professor started flaming me!

From that point I just lost interest in Bayanihan.....They claim to have PCs sold in a shop in SM Manila with Bayanihan preinstalled...I have not seen this so I can't confirm...

Anyway for para sa mga Kabayan ko na nagtatanong...There is a Pilipino Linux Users Group(plug)....As a OFW I have no idea how active this group is....but at least it exists.

### Post by Jucato on 2007-08-04
> **bme said:**
> People on that team had the nerve to ask for pasalubong whenever I get home(perhaps a joke?).
It's a common Filipino friendly joke to ask for pasalubong from people coming home from far places (a.k.a. a different province), even if you just met him/her a few hours ago. Don't take it too seriously. :)

> Then that professor started flaming me!
Of course, this is not a joke... 

> There is a Pilipino Linux Users Group(plug)....As a OFW I have no idea how active this group is....but at least it exists.

They're quite active from what I've seen. But I think they're too busy being active in arguing to make any inroads in FOSS in our country... I'm not a member of PLUG, nor do I aspire to be. It's too scary to be in their mailing list... just IMHO...:confused:

### Post by chimp_rex on 2007-08-07
> **Nessa said:**
> Share naman po ng link to a wine installation how-to thread that worked for you...

Hi Nessa!

1. Open Terminal

2. Add Wine Repository to your sources list:

wget -q [http://wine.budgetdedicated.com/apt/387EE263.gpg](http://wine.budgetdedicated.com/apt/387EE263.gpg) -O- | sudo apt-key add -
sudo wget [http://wine.budgetdedicated.com/apt/sources.list.d/feisty.list](http://wine.budgetdedicated.com/apt/sources.list.d/feisty.list) -O /etc/apt/sources.list.d/winehq.list
sudo apt-get update

3. Install wine

sudo apt-get install wine

4. To run Wine in Windows terminal:

wine program.exe

====
You can also do this GUI-style in Synaptic. But I prefer terminal kasi mas mabilis. Good luck!

---

### Post by wersdaluv on 2007-08-07
> **Nessa said:**
> Share naman po ng link to a wine installation how-to thread that worked for you...

Add mo sa sources.list mo yung repo ng wine by entering ```
sudo gedit /etc/apt/sources.list
```
Tapos, add mo sa file na yon ito
```
# Upstream Wine
# GPG key: 387EE263
deb http://wine.budgetdedicated.com/apt feisty main
```

Tapos, ```

sudo apt-get install wine
```

O kaya, sa Add/Remove, search mo wine tapos tick the check box.

Pwede rin sa Synaptic. Search mo wine tapos install mo dun.

### Post by pinoyskull on 2007-08-10
> **gina88 said:**
> Ubuntu rin me (dual boot nga lang)!!!
wahaha pati dito sa pinas may ubuntu!! tanong lang...
pano gumamit ng installer sa ubuntu? nagdl ako ng Audacity installer (sure ko its for linux, .deb ata ung extension)  from windoze pero hindi ko alam ano gagawin pagdating ko sa ubuntu.

Open your file browser and point it to the directory where you put your .deb file, then double click on it, **gDebi Package Installer** will install it for you...

or if you want it in CLI mode, go to the directory of your .deb file then issue the command

```
sudo dpkg -i myinstaller.deb
```

---

### Post by wersdaluv on 2007-08-10
> **gina88 said:**
> nagdl ako ng Audacity installer (sure ko its for linux, .deb ata ung extension)  from windoze pero hindi ko alam ano gagawin pagdating ko sa ubuntu.

Pre, karamihan ng kailangan mo, nasa repositories na ng Ubuntu (see [https://help.ubuntu.com/community/Repositories/Ubuntu](https://help.ubuntu.com/community/Repositories/Ubuntu))

So kung audacity lang din, just ```
sudo apt-get install audacity
```

### Post by loell on 2007-08-20
kung na install mo na ang nvidia driver na para sa linux,

pwede kanang gummamit nang nvidia settings tool.

para mag install nang nvidia settings tool, sa command line terminal, type mo lang

```
sudo apt-get install nvidia-settings 
```

pagkatapos mong mag install , ang program ay makikita  sa

**Applications Menu --> System Tools Menu --> Nvidia**

doon pwede mong e-adjust ang gamma , brightness, etc.

### Post by loell on 2007-08-21
walang mali sa ginawa mo :)

tanong ko lang , na install mo na ba properly ang nividia driver mo?
anong exactong pangalan nang card mo?

sabi nang nvidia settings mo.

```
ERROR: NV-CONTROL extension not found on this Display.
```

kaya malamang hindi mo , na install ang ```
nvidia-glx
``` or ```
nvidia-glx-new
``` drivers.

para hindi ka mahirapan, punta ka sa

**Systems Menu --> Administration --> Restricted Drivers Manager**

input ang password mo, tapos e-enable mo ang nvidia accelerated Driver , basta check mo lang ang check box, para ma install.

restart mo ang pc, tapos balik ka sa nvidia-settings. :)

### Post by wersdaluv on 2007-08-27
> **loell said:**
> walang problema sa pag-mamanage nang loco forum, wala namang pinoy na sobrang pasaway diba? :biggrin:

kaya kahit sinong member sa official loco team, ok na yun.

Pwede tayo magrequest.

kailangan lang >  1. Please make sure your project is listed on the LoCo team wiki here: [https://wiki.ubuntu.com/LoCoTeamList](https://wiki.ubuntu.com/LoCoTeamList)
 2. What subdomain prefix do you want. example: (prefix.ubuntuforums.org)
 3. What is your LoCo team name
 4. The forum user(s) (max 2) who will be the moderator for your forum
 5. Please make sure you are the registered contact person for this LoCo Team as per the listing on the [https://wiki.ubuntu.com/LoCoTeamList](https://wiki.ubuntu.com/LoCoTeamList) wiki page

So isip na lang tay ng subdomain prefix, LoCo team name at kung sino mga willing na mods. WIlling ako maging mod dito pero hindi ako willing na ako magmanage. Para sa number 5, kailangan nga yata natin siguro si Mr. Jerome.

### Post by Jucato on 2007-08-30
Mga kababayan,

Ibabahagi ko lang po yung e-mail na pinadala ko sa Ubuntu-PH mailing list na humihingi ng opinyon tungkol sa mungkahing bagbukas ng isang sub-forum dito. Inilapit ko na ang mungkahing ito kay zakame (Zak Elep) at napag-isipan naming tanungin din ang ibang miyembro ng Ubuntu-PH. Eto ang nilalaman ng e-mail:

> Good day!

There has been a proposal from the Filipino member of the Ubuntuforums to 
request a Filipino sub-forum there: 
[http://u1buntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=68805&page=138](http://u1buntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=68805&page=138)

We already have our own forum (Drupal) in [http://ubuntu-ph.org](http://ubuntu-ph.org) which already 
existed before Ubuntuforums.org started to offer sub-forums for LoCo teams. 
The thread(s) for Pinoy Users have been in Ubuntuforums.org for quite some 
time now. The activity on ubuntu-ph.org has also been very low, but recently 
there have been new posts, which might conflict with one of the requirements 
for requesting a LoCo sub-forum: 
[http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=290685](http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=290685)

I'm bringing this proposal to the members of the community, so that we could 
discuss and decide what to do, given some of the pros and cons listed below. 
Zak, being the current LoCo contact, will be the one to formally request for 
the forum. I'm proposing loell ( [http://ubuntuforums.org/member.php?u=44017](http://ubuntuforums.org/member.php?u=44017) ) 
and myself as moderators for the sub-forum.

Advantages of having an Ubuntuforums.org sub-forum:
1. We can worry less about infrastructure, maintenance and administration of 
forums and more on doing what we should be doing, like projects, information 
dissemination, etc.

2. Time-tested and proven forum system. We can take advantage of what 
Ubuntuforums.org has already built upon.

3. More visibility, easier access to information, and wider audience. Very few 
people know about ubuntu-ph.org. Most new Ubuntu users also probably go to 
Ubuntuforums.org more. And searching for information in that forums will also 
yield more results, given they have a bigger knowledge base.

Disadvantages would include:
1. Multiple entry points, multiple user accounts. It would have been very 
ideal if we all just had to access one site for all our LoCo resources, and 
only needed one user account per person.

2. No direct control. We would be practically giving up control over the forum 
and those who would be users of that forum.

3. We already have our own forums, although activity has been sparse and 
sporadic. But the reason it is less activity is because it is less known. And 
it is less known because it is less used, even by people who already know it 
exists (mea culpa). I already did try to "advertise" the existence of the 
ubuntu-ph.org forum, but the response was not enough, specially considering 
there are people who are already members of Ubuntuforums.org who would find 
it inconvenient or impractical to be at two places.

Looking forward to the suggestions of the community. Thanks!


- Jucato

Sa kasamaang palad, kakaunti pa lang ang nagbibigay ng kanilang boto. Sa kabutihang palad naman, ang 3 ito ay mga opisyal na miyembro ng Ubuntu (Ubuntu members). Sa makatuwid, maaaring magkaroon tayo ng sub-forum natin dito.

P.S. Hindi ako nagbigay ng boto ko kasi ako ang naglapit sa kanila ng mungkahi. Conflict of interest kung baga. Hehehe. :guitar:

EDIT: Medyo kakapalan ng mukha na nagvolunteer ako maging moderator. Si loell ang sinuggest ko kasi matagal ko na siyang kilala dito. Kaso di pa siya masyadong kilala ng ibang Ubuntu-PH/Ubuntu members kaya baka mahirapan magpaalam. Sana wag ninyo masamain. :)

---

### Post by loell on 2007-09-05
basically any sip softphone can do this through gtalk2voip service

i made a a howto awhile back [URL="http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=414121"]   	
HOWTO: Voice call Yahoo Messenger using Ekiga and gtalk2voip service.[/URL]


in gizmoproject 3.0  though , some of the process are automated

first download the latest gizmo deb package at [www.gizmoproject.com/download.php]("www.gizmoproject.com/download.php")

launch gizmo and define your account if you haven't.

now go to [http://www.gtalk2voip.com/](http://www.gtalk2voip.com/) , put your yahoo contact's name and press invite , that person will recieve a buddy invite which she/he must accept in order for you to call. the buddy name that he/she'll be accepting is **ie (gtalk2voip003@yahoo.com or [email]gtalk2voip004@yahoo.com[/email] , etc **

after your contacts accepts it, you can then call them, just type or add it as one of your contact in gizmoproject, example **john_doe@yahoo.com** then press the call icon, wait for a moment as it is routed by gtalk2voip service to YM.

### Post by daxumaming on 2007-09-20
I would just like to inform everyone that there's been a proposal regarding 

1) killing the Ubuntu-ph.org/forum and move to Ubuntuforums.org
or
2) retaining the Ubuntu-ph.org/forum

### Post by daxumaming on 2007-09-22
Ubuntu-PH Members;

Discussion for Ubuntu-PH Logo is now Open. So is the Submission of Artwork and Voting.  We welcome all kinds of artwork, however, you should adhere to the Logo Usage Guidelines as listed in the Trademark Policy [1]. We currently have 2 candidate logos and if you're an artist and would like to submit your work, then please upload it to the wiki[2] or send it to me or Jucato[3].

How to vote:
Just add your name under the candidate logo. You can only vote once, but you are allowed to change your vote as artworks are submitted.

Details are listed on the wiki[2].

Thank you

[1] [http://www.ubuntu.com/aboutus/trademarkpolicy](http://www.ubuntu.com/aboutus/trademarkpolicy)
[2] [http://ubuntu-ph.org/wiki/Projects/Logo](http://ubuntu-ph.org/wiki/Projects/Logo)
[3] jucato at kubuntu.org

### Post by Jucato on 2007-10-16
yeah di masyadong mahilig mag forums si Zak, pero lagi sya sa IRC channel natin. Kaya sinasabi na lang naman kung may importanteng kailangang sabihin. Welcome din kayo sa IRC channel syempre. Ingat nga lang, nakakaadik ang IRC para sa ibang tao. :D

Siya ang LoCo (Local Community) contact person ng buong Ubuntu-Ph. So kapag may kailangan ang Ubuntu-Ph from the larger Ubuntu community (like CD's, materials, permissions, resources, etc.) siya ang naglalakad. Tulad nitong subforum natin, sya ang nag-official request.

---

### Post by kopinux on 2007-10-19
install copy paste sa terminal
[COLOR="Red"]apt-get install wine[/COLOR]

to run
[COLOR="Red"]wine setup.exe[/COLOR]

andami na din palang mmorpg na pwede sa linux ano, dapat pala pinapauso ito ng mga internet cafe.
gawa sila ng linux pc na may mga linux mmorpg.

### Post by Samhain13 on 2007-10-25
> **kopinux said:**
> flash 8 yata. nakita ko kay Samhain, isa sa mga member dito sa video nya na may pinaandar siyang flash 8.

Na-install ko dati yung Flash 8 Professional sa Wine pero may mga .dll pa akong ni-download para umandar siya. Nakalimutan ko lang kung ano talaga-- hindi ko pa ulit nilalagay kasi yung Flash simula nag-clean install ako ng Gutsy. (At wala na akong balak ilagay pa yun, hehehehe!)

Anyway, malalaman naman yun sa Terminal kasi sasabihin na may .dll na "cannot be found". So Google na lang para sa mga .dll na yun. Kung tama ang pagkakaalala ko, dalawang .dll yun. Hindi naman mahirap hanapin.

### Post by Samhain13 on 2007-10-30
The Adobe Creative Suite applications are normally not supported but I've been able to install the CS1 version of Photoshop under Wine. I believe the other applications from that version are also usable under Wine already.

Of course, there are alternatives to those applications. But then again, they are operated in such a different manner as the Adobe applications that they make amateurs of seemingly long-time professionals.

(Sorry for the rant, I'm just tired of reading stuff like "Gimp is ages behind Photoshop" from folks who seem to think that their familiarity in PS is somewhat a benchmark on their professional abilities. Ehehe!)

Blender3D is available in the repositories, but like the other alternatives, it will take some getting-used-to. And Bryce, I believe (although I can't remember where I've read it), is also available in Linux. :D

---

### Post by Samhain13 on 2007-10-31
> **zyg0t3 said:**
> I'm just curious but, are you guys graphic designers? or 3d designers? I'd be interested in knowing how many people out there who do design work professionally  (as the main source of income) and work on a regular basis use linux and the design apps that are available there. (ports, hacks, native apps, etc.)

I'm a web designer by trade and have been freelancing since early 2005. My work involves some image processing, primarily in preparing graphics files for use in the Web. I also occasionally accept graphic design for print but I consider that, or what I do regarding that, a minor spin-off of my primary trade.

However, I have prior experience in companies as a graphic designer: as a pre-press artist and illustrator in a printing press, a cover artist in two recording companies; and as a Flash multimedia artist/developer and web designer in an IT company. I have also had shots at video editing and very basic sound mixing. These experiences involve working on both Windows and Macintosh.

And yes, for a year now I've been using the Gimp and Inkscape-- combining their functionalities for filling one or the other's shortcomings when compared to Adobe or Corel graphics applications. For repetitive image manipulation tasks like resizing, enhancing and thumbnailing multiple files, I use ImageMagick in conjunction with simple bash scripts (that I am still learning how to write properly). Scribus is something that I also would love to have a grip on, and we'll get to that as work demands.

I have also been able to use Flash 8 Professional (in Ubuntu) for a couple of projects late last year but I don't offer those services any more (now exploring other possibilities).

:)

Welcome Lorsban.

---

### Post by Samhain13 on 2007-11-02
> **zyg0t3 said:**
> @Samhain

So you've been doing full time graphic work on Linux huh? That's impressive. How was the learning curve and what do you find lacking or that you wish would carry over from mac or win to lin?

I tried working with gimpshop for a few days but didn't have the longevity to stick with it. Also i hate that you have to hack (WINE or vmware) linux to get window versions of programs, i find them to be very unstable.

The learning curve wasn't as stiff for me because even when I had Windows as my primary OS, I was already giving time to learning GIMP and Blender (both are available in Widows). Although it's been a while now since I touched the latter.

The thing that I miss in the GIMP, of course, is CMYK mode, which is needed if the output was for print. As I understand, the new version of GIMP already has this although I have not explored this new function yet. It's been a while now since I was required to produce anything that needs to be in CMYK.

GIMPshop, I haven't tried yet. Hehehe, and I'm honestly not interested in it. :) I know that it was designed for hardcore PS users, to help ease the migration from PS to GIMP but, as I've said, I've used GIMP along side PS before so I guess I don't belong to GIMPshop's target users.

Regarding Wine, the latest versions of Windows programs available in it, I think, will always be unstable. So the best recourse is to use slightly older versions while waiting for the latest ones to become stable-- unless, of course, one enjoys hacking. If you're strictly an Adobe user, the first CS version seems to run fine. I was able to use PS CS1 without hassle for a couple of months last year, it's quite stable. Also Flash 8 Pro. You should visit WineHQ for more information regarding this, there are a lot of solutions available there.

:)

---

**01:00.0 VGA compatible controller: ATI Technologies Inc M9+ 5C61 [Radeon Mobility 9200 (AGP)] (rev 01)**
dual boot ako yung Motogp3 playable naman dun sa WindowsXP dun sa ubuntu nag run siya gamit yung wine kaya lang super bagal. saka yung America's army ambagal din lalo na dun sa mga SF maps gaya ng Urban Assault, d ko pa na try yung America's Army sa WindowsXP.

### Post by loell on 2008-01-30
yes, unfortunately its a common problem, most probably a bug in compiz fusion, try this though. 
in gconf-editor, apps->gnome-screensaver--> theme field , set it to **blank-only**

### Post by loell on 2008-07-22
welcome po dito, **pitirpol** :)

mukhang ma auto-detect naman sa ubuntu yung **Epson C59**

subukan mong i-configure sa **System** menu -->**Administration** --> **Printing**


edit-- looking at your first post, malamang sinubukan mo nang mag configure nang  printer, di ba na detect?



atsaka yung **Motorola Z3** , pag may data cable ka, ubuntu will just identify it as a storage device.

### Post by lutosdemayo on 2008-12-28
> **Rome.konig said:**
> hello friends, do you guys know of any programs or app, that can host a server for networking like windows media player so i can open files on my ps3? when i updated my ubuntu i accidentally screwed up my grub menu.lst and windows wont boot anymore. I mainly use windows for media player because it can host a server and my playstation 3 can pick it up through lan. any suggestions? 
thank you! maraming salamat! go pacquiao!!!

if you are looking for just a file server why dont u use ubuntu instead using samba. You can start here [http://www.watchingthenet.com/enable-file-sharing-in-ubuntu-using-samba.html](http://www.watchingthenet.com/enable-file-sharing-in-ubuntu-using-samba.html) or you can just reinstall grub and start here [https://help.ubuntu.com/community/RecoveringUbuntuAfterInstallingWindows](https://help.ubuntu.com/community/RecoveringUbuntuAfterInstallingWindows) so that u can use windows again.:):P

Cheers mate!

### Post by killer_d76 on 2010-05-12
I just installed **10.04** on our lappie.. it's blazing fast in my own opinion, but for some reason it can't seem to mount all of my USB storage device!... from External HDD to USB Flash Drive!... usb mouse and Huawei USB modem works perfectly though?.. patulong naman oh... thanks!

---

### Post by e30ernest on 2010-05-12
> **killer_d76 said:**
> I just installed **10.04** on our lappie.. it's blazing fast in my own opinion, but for some reason it can't seem to mount all of my USB storage device!... from External HDD to USB Flash Drive!... usb mouse and Huawei USB modem works perfectly though?.. patulong naman oh... thanks!

```
sudo apt-get install ntfs-config
```

then:
```
sudo ntfs-config
```

Enable read and write to both internal and external ntfs drives. :)

I hope this helps.

---

### Post by apolloltiujr on 2010-09-15
Sun, Smart, or Globe Broadband on Ubuntu 10.04


If  you are using Sun Broadband Wireless (tested on Huawei E1550) and want  it to work on Ubuntu 10.04 (Lucid Lynx), just install the  linux-backports-modules-headers-lucid-generic package and the  usb-modeswitch package.view plainprint?   


$ sudo apt-get install linux-backports-modules-headers-lucid-generic usb-modeswitch


After installing, reboot.


Plug  in the Sun Broadband. Then, a notification “New Mobile Broadband  Connection” should appear. Follow the wizard dialog (you can just click  next since the default values should be alright). Then, you should be  connected now.


Connection Name: Digitel (Sun Cellular) Connection


Mobile: *99#
Username:
Password:


Advance 
APN: fbband
Network:
Pin:&#65279;

---

### Post by apolloltiujr on 2010-09-15
> **zeee said:**
> Ayos! Daming Pinoy! :D

Have been using Ubuntu Lucid Lynx for almost two months now.. I'm using Windows for programming na lang, visual studio kasi. Nagsasanay pa sa Ubuntu programming tools. Hehe. 

Pero besides from that, lahat Ubuntu na! ;)

Dont worry you can still used some Windows Based Program on Ubuntu 10.04 by installing Wine... Application + Ubuntu Software + Search for "Wine"

Even Play Starcraft, Warcraft, Red Alert, or used your Adobe Photo shop can run.
I've Tested since I used to run  *Ubuntu* 8.04.4 LTS (*Hardy* Heron)

Its Cool even used a Old PC 
Ubuntu Desktop (GUI) Installation

    * 1 GHz x86 processor
    * 512 MiB of system memory (RAM)
    * 5 GB of disk space (for OS files; consideration should be given to the (often very large) size of user files that will occupy the /home directory)
    * Graphics card and monitor capable of 1024x768
    * Cd/Dvd-drive
    * Sound support, if you need sound.
    * Internet access is helpful 

And Linux can not be affected any Virus.
The Security more powerful than  Windows based program.
